FULL TEASER TREATMENTS — COMPLETE TEXT
================================================================


----------------------------------------------------------------
TEASER ONE: AMERICAN FREEDOM
----------------------------------------------------------------

AMERICAN FREEDOM
Campaign Teaser — Full Treatment
Music: "Good Morning America" — Jesse Welles

FORMAT
Runtime: approx. 90 seconds
No dialogue. No HUD. No gameplay footage.
Aspect ratio: 2.39:1 cinematic widescreen
Grade: desaturated, cool morning light, high contrast shadows

---

ACT ONE — RECOGNITION
0:00 — 0:20

Black screen. Silence. Two full beats.

The first guitar notes of Good Morning America come in barely
audible — like a radio signal finding its frequency from a long
way away.

Image fades in slowly. Pre-dawn blue light. The camera drifts
forward at roof height, unhurried, almost floating, down what is
unmistakably a Main Street in small-town America. Storefronts.
A diner with its lights still off. A church steeple against a
pale sky. Fall foliage. It looks almost peaceful.

The camera drifts lower.

A Russian military checkpoint fills the intersection ahead.
A BTR parked across two lanes. Soldiers in unfamiliar uniforms,
breath visible in the cold morning air. A Russian flag hanging
from a telephone pole, completely still.

No dramatic sting. No music swell. Just that image, held long
enough to land.

---

ACT TWO — WEIGHT
0:20 — 0:50

The camera keeps moving — slow, documentary, without commentary.
We see the town in fragments.

A shuttered hardware store, plywood boards spray-painted with a
message in English. A burned-out house, two or three survivors
and neighbors quietly picking through the wreckage in the early
light, shovels moving slowly. A child's face at a curtained
window watching a patrol pass below. A handwritten sign in a
shop window in English and Russian. An elderly man sitting on
his porch steps, hands folded, watching nothing in particular.

Jesse Welles' voice carries the melody. The music still sounds
like home. The images don't look like home anymore. The contrast
does the emotional work without comment.

One image held a beat longer than the others: a partially burned
American flag still hanging from a porch railing, moving almost
imperceptibly in the morning cold.

No comment. Just that.

---

ACT THREE — CURRENT
0:50 — 1:10

The music begins to shift — not into anything loud, just a subtle
change in emotional register underneath the melody, like something
waking up.

Quick cuts. Still no dialogue.

A hand pressing a magazine into a rifle in near-darkness.
Mud-caked boots moving along a treeline. A face — Romeo's,
half-lit by weak morning light — watching a patrol pass from
cover, completely still. A resistance contact sliding a folded
paper across a table without making eye contact. A flare climbing
into a grey sky somewhere in the middle distance. Shadowed figures
moving with quiet urgency through the back of a barn.

Buried here, in the momentum of the cuts, lasting approximately
three frames:

THE CODY BEAUMONT IMAGE.

Not dwelt upon. Not explained. Gone before the conscious mind can
fully form the question. Something is wrong with what you just saw.
You're not sure what.

The cuts continue. Nothing acknowledges it.

Romeo again — moving now, low and deliberate through undergrowth,
toward the edge of a tree line.

---

ACT FOUR — RECKONING
1:10 — 1:28

The quick cuts stop.

One wide, still shot: Romeo at the top of a hill, standing at the
edge of the tree line. His back is to the camera. He is looking
down at the town below — the checkpoints, the unfamiliar flags,
the smoke from a chimney here and there, ordinary life ground down
to its most essential and most fragile.

He doesn't move.

The guitar melody of Good Morning America begins to fall away —
and in its place, quietly at first and then with full weight, the
same melody rises again in unaccompanied human voices. A mixed
choir, sparse and unhurried, somewhere between a hymn and a
lament. The tonal reference is the Civil War vocal tradition —
voices that sound like they belong to the land, not to a recording
studio. The melody has grown larger than one man with a guitar.
It belongs to everyone in that town now.

Romeo still doesn't move.

---

CLOSE
1:28 — 1:35

Hard cut to black.

The choir stops mid-phrase.

Silence. One full beat.

---

White text. Plain. No fanfare. No musical swell beneath it.

WAR HITS HOME.

One beat.

AMERICAN FREEDOM.

One beat.

Coming Q2 2028.

Fade.

---
Treatment v1.0 — Sidebar Development File
Main narrative authority: primary project thread


----------------------------------------------------------------
TEASER TWO: AEGIS FALLS
----------------------------------------------------------------

AEGIS FALLS
Campaign Teaser — Full Treatment
Music: "Kyiv" — Apashe ft. Alina Pash

FORMAT
Runtime: approx. 90 seconds
No dialogue. No HUD. No gameplay footage.
Aspect ratio: 2.39:1 cinematic widescreen
Grade: cold, high contrast, deep shadows — steel blue and amber
where light exists
Visual grammar: two modes — cinematic widescreen and raw
POV/drone footage. POV material is ungraded, aspect ratio native
to source, audio authentic. The two grammars are kept visually
distinct at all times.

---

ACT ONE — THE PROMISE
0:00 — 0:15

Black. Then Alina Pash's voice comes in alone — just the vocal,
unaccompanied, in Ukrainian. No orchestration yet. The language
sounds simultaneously foreign and deeply familiar to Western ears.
Beautiful and melancholy and completely unafraid.

A single image fades in slowly against it.

The AEGIS emblem. Clean and sharp, rendered in the established
briefing screen aesthetic — dark background, gold and silver
insignia, the Latin motto beneath it.

Recte Faciendo Neminem Timeas.

It looks authoritative. Trustworthy. Like something that has never
failed and has no reason to expect that it will.

Hold on it. Let Alina Pash's voice carry it.

Then cut to black.

---

ACT TWO — THE WEIGHT
0:15 — 0:50

The orchestration begins to build underneath the vocal, slowly,
with intention.

All footage in this section is cinematic. No POV material yet.

Geography established through feeling rather than labels. The flat
grey expanse of the North Sea at night, surface broken by wind.
The massive industrial silhouette of Rotterdam's port infrastructure
against a low sky. The angular geometry of a communications relay
station surrounded by deep Arctic snow — we don't name it Svalbard,
but the cold names it for us. Wet cobblestones in a European city
at night, boots moving with controlled urgency.

Then the operational texture. AEGIS in environments that should be
controlled but aren't quite behaving that way. A door that opens
onto something unexpected, a beat of stillness before the operator
moves. A contact who isn't where they're supposed to be. A screen
showing data that contradicts the brief. Frost at a tall window,
mask on, completely still, watching something below that the camera
does not show us. Ducky on a radio, expression unreadable,
listening to something we cannot hear.

Woven between these — brief, almost incidental — the details that
are wrong underneath the surface. A name visible on a document for
just long enough to register. A timestamp that doesn't add up if
you're paying attention. A familiar face in a place it has no
business being.

Nothing explained. Everything felt.

The music continues to build. Alina Pash's voice rising, the
orchestration thickening and broadening around it.

We return to the AEGIS emblem.

The same image. But there is a crack running through it now —
hairline thin, barely visible, easy to dismiss as a trick of the
light. The motto still perfectly legible beneath it.

Cut away before the viewer has fully decided what they saw.

---

ACT THREE — THE FRACTURE
0:50 — 1:10

The music hits its first real peak. The teaser shifts register.

This is where the raw POV material enters for the first time —
and its arrival is felt precisely because the first two acts earned
it. A burst of helmet-mounted GoPro footage, ungraded, slightly
blown out, the audio raw and immediate. Combat in a European
industrial environment, close and fast and without the composed
geometry of cinematic framing. Then back to cinematic. Then raw
again, slightly longer this time. Then cinematic. The alternation
accelerates in sync with the music — the two grammars trading
places with increasing frequency as the build intensifies, until
near the peak they are cutting against each other almost measure
for measure.

The raw footage carries that specific visual grammar of modern
warfare as people actually know it now. Drone footage, the eerie
detached silence of it before impact. Night vision green. Thermal
white-hot signatures of vehicles moving through darkness. A
handheld shot of a street engagement, audio blown out by nearby
concussion. The intimacy and inhumanity existing in the same frame
simultaneously.

Interspersed with both grammars — the operational reality of what
is going wrong. AEGIS in cover in an environment that was supposed
to be friendly. Ducky making a decision we don't understand with
information we don't have. Frost firing from a position that tells
us the plan has already failed. Switchblade pulling someone out of
a collapsing space, not looking up, focused entirely on the person
in her hands.

The question the campaign is actually asking moves underneath all
of it, never surfaced directly, only accumulated:

Who built this. Who funded it. Who does it actually serve.

The music reaches its peak — and then hollows out. The
orchestration falls away beneath Alina Pash's voice, leaving her
exposed and solitary and completely clear.

The raw POV footage recedes with the orchestration. The last few
cuts are cinematic again — stilled, composed. The visual grammar
settling back into itself as the music does.

---

ACT FOUR — THE RECKONING
1:10 — 1:28

One final image, held steady against that lone vocal.

The AEGIS emblem. Third and final time.

It is fractured now. Not destroyed — fractured. The crack from
before has spread across the face of the shield in a spider web
pattern, the way safety glass breaks — still holding its shape,
still recognizable as what it was, the structure intact but
fundamentally and irreversibly compromised. Every line of the
insignia still visible. The motto still legible beneath it.

Recte Faciendo Neminem Timeas.

Hold on it. Let Alina Pash carry the silence around it.

Then cut to black. The vocal stops.

Silence. One full beat.

---

White text. Plain. No fanfare.

THE SYSTEM FELL.

One beat.

WE DIDN'T.

One beat.

AEGIS FALLS.

One beat.

Coming Q2 2028.

Fade.

---
Treatment v1.0 — Sidebar Development File
Main narrative authority: primary project thread

Flag for revision when Persistent Threat (Ducky Game 2) mission
geography is developed in main narrative thread.


----------------------------------------------------------------
TEASER THREE: GODKILLER
----------------------------------------------------------------

GODKILLER
Campaign Teaser — Full Treatment
Music: "King Nothing" — Metallica

FORMAT
Runtime: approx. 90 seconds
Minimal dialogue — two lines at close only.
No HUD. No gameplay footage.
Aspect ratio: 2.39:1 cinematic widescreen
Grade: high contrast, deep shadows, warm amber and cold white
where artificial light exists — the palette of late nights in
rooms where important things are decided and never recorded

---

ACT ONE — THE FILE
0:00 — 0:20

Black. Silence.

King Nothing begins — not the opening riff, but the single breath
of anticipation just before it. One beat of quiet that makes the
guitar's arrival inevitable.

Then the riff hits and we open on:

A pair of hands — Spook's — laying a photograph face up on a
table in a dark room. We don't see his face yet. Just the hands,
and the photograph, and a pool of artificial light falling across
a surface covered in documents, strings, photographs, case files.
The architecture of an investigation that has been running for a
long time and has not yet found its floor.

The photograph is of Goldberg. Composed. Confident. The face of
a man who has never been held accountable for anything and has no
expectation that this will change.

Below the photograph, stamped in red:

DECEASED.

Spook's hand rests on the photograph for a moment. Still. Then he
slides it to one side and keeps working.

He doesn't believe it either.

---

ACT TWO — THE TRAIL
0:20 — 0:55

King Nothing drives this section. The music has momentum and the
teaser uses it.

We move through the world of the campaign in quick, kinetic cuts —
but always refracted through the specific lens of intelligence
work rather than conventional action. This is not Romeo's war.
This is not Ducky's institutional crisis. This is the world as
seen through surveillance, through intercepted documents, through
the gap between what the official record says and what is actually
true underneath it.

Fragments. Locations felt rather than named or labeled. Rain-
slicked streets of a European city at night, headlights smearing
across wet stone. The interior of a safehouse lived in for too
long — takeout containers, multiple laptops, a corkboard dense
with material. An airport concourse, Spook and his team moving
through the civilian flow like ghosts, unhurried, invisible.
A skyscraper face at night, a figure rappelling down glass toward
a lit window below. A tropical compound perimeter at night,
security lights cutting hard lines through the dark.

Interspersed with the locations — the paper trail. Fragments of
documents, never held long enough to fully read. Photographs with
names partially visible. Redacted lines that confirm something is
present without revealing what. A name appearing across multiple
separate files in separate contexts, connecting things that should
have no connection.

And woven through all of it — faces. Goldberg. Stockbridge.
Macmillan. Crodyn. Each appearing briefly, never labeled, never
explained. Simply present. Watching from inside their photographs
and their files with the particular composure of people who have
never had reason to be afraid of being seen.

Then a cut that lands differently than the ones around it:

A television screen. News broadcast, slightly grainy. A chyron
running beneath footage of a federal prison facility. We cannot
read it fully — only fragments. Explosion. Federal facility.
One confirmed dead.

Then the photograph of Goldberg again. Different photograph.
Same stamp.

DECEASED.

Spook's face for the first time — lit from below by the cold
light of a screen, expression unreadable, somewhere between fury
and something that might almost be recognition. The look of a man
who has just been told a joke he already knew the punchline to
and is not remotely amused by it.

---

ACT THREE — THE HUNT
0:55 — 1:15

The music moves into its harder register and the teaser opens up.

Brief, controlled glimpses of action — not sustained sequences,
just enough to establish what is at stake and what these men are
willing to do to reach it. A close quarters engagement in a dark
interior, fast and without ceremony. Spook moving through a
burning space with the unhurried focus of a man looking for
something specific amid the chaos. Tripper at a keyboard inside
a vehicle moving fast through a city at night. Smoke back against
a wall beside a doorway, covering the approach, waiting.

But the action is never the point here. Every action beat is
interrupted by or resolves into another intelligence fragment —
another piece of the picture assembling itself into something
larger and more dangerous than any single mission.

Until one cut that arrives without announcement and sits longer
than everything around it:

East McFarlane Island. Wide aerial shot, golden hour light, the
water around it the deep blue of somewhere that does not appear
on maps that ordinary people consult. Isolated. Beautiful.
Completely self-contained.

Then Goldberg — alive. Standing at the edge of a terrace
overlooking the water, back partially to camera, unhurried,
looking at the horizon with the posture of a man who has decided
he is entirely beyond reach. No urgency. No fear. Just a man
standing on his island in the golden hour, watching the water.

Then black. Sudden and total.

---

ACT FOUR — THE EXCHANGE
1:15 — 1:28

The music strips back to almost nothing. Just the guitar, quiet.

Spook's voice — low, flat, certain. The only spoken words in
the teaser:

"You can't kill a dead man."

A beat of silence.

Then another voice — older, quieter, somewhere in the register
of a man who finds most things faintly amusing and has learned
not to show it too obviously:

"No."

Cut to black. Music stops completely.

Silence. One full beat.

---

White text. Plain. No fanfare. No music beneath it.

YOU CAN'T KILL A DEAD MAN.

One beat.

GODKILLER.

One beat.

Coming Q2 2028.

Fade.

---

Fictional FPS campaign, pt. I
Prompt:
I am looking to write a fictional Call of Duty-style three-campaign fps storyline.
The setting is a fictional present-day global conflict. The story is told through the intertwining storylines of the three playable main characters, each
from a different background, and takes the player to a number of locations worldwide; from Frankfurt, Germany to Tokyo, Japan, southern Poland,
the eastern Mediterranean, and US locations including Utah, the Pacific Northwest, downtown LA, and naval bases in southwestern California.
The story centers on a conspiracy of a paramilitary group of unknown malicious actors that culminates in a catastrophic cyber attack on the US, and
several Western-aligned countries across the world in which automated military air and ground drones systems are taken over and turned against the
American citizens.
The three campaigns show three different perspectives of the conflict:
Campaign 1:
Critter Squad
LT Ramón "Romeo" Álvarez
Fire Team Delta - US Army 75th Ranger Regiment
Romeo, the Fire Team leader and his squad mates, callsigns Dingo, Howler, and Beaver, are deployed to eastern Poland to shore up defences at the
eastern NATO border against an anticipated Russian invasion attempt.
The ensuing cyber attack and turn of events sees Fire Team Delta escaping Russian encirclement near the southern border of Poland, evading drones,
and moving through eastern Czech republic and Austria to Germany to regroup with US and NATO forces at Ramstein Air Base.
Afterwards, Romeo and his squad are sent to team up with AEGIS Squad to protect classified geospatial intelligence infrastructure installations
located at sites in the Faroe islands, deep in the French Alps, on the remote Greek island of Lemnos in the Aegean Sea, and near the West-Frisian
town of Hinderloopen in the North of the Netherlands. In the final act of the campaign, command contacts Romeo over satellite phone and orders his
squad to return stateside immediately to help defend the US West Coast from an amphibious invasion by what appears to be a coalition of Russian,
North Korean, and Iranian forces. With all flights grounded due to the cyber attack, Fire Team Delta, with help from AEGIS Squad, make their way
across the Breton countryside to the French Naval Base at the Île Longue peninsula in Brittany where they help intercept an enemy sabotage
operation against the French garrison base and two nuclear french submarines stationed on location, Le Terrible, and Le Vigilant. Upon foiling the
enemy sabotage attempt and securing the garrison, AEGIS Squad are diverted to fight Russian invasion forces alongside a detachment of Dutch
Marine Corps troops at the Maasvlakte Oil and Gas terminal in the port of Rotterdam to protect it from destruction by enemy special forces. Romeo
and his team secure a rendezvous with the nuclear submersible USS District of Columbia who offer Romeo's team passage to the US West Coast. Due
to ongoing naval blockade attempts by invading forces, the District of Columbia surfaces off the coast of Ventura, California, and the squad are able
to make contact with a US army infantry detachment stationed inside the city.
The troops are en route to join a detachment of Marines at the Port of Los Angeles in Long Beach, and headed to clear the towns along the Ventura
Freeway between Oxnard and Burbank. Romeo's squad agree to join them.
The troops reach the city of Los Angeles from the northwest and enter the city through North Hollywood.
On their way to Long Beach they help push North Korean invading forces out of North Hollywood (Down Rodeo) and the South of Beverly Hills
towards the coast.
The troops eventually reach the Port of Los Angeles, and find it securely occupied by a platoon of US Marines. According to the platoon CO, forward
observers report that the invading DPRK forces are preparing to seize the Long Beach Airport.
The squad and the rest of the Soldiers and Marines determine to stop them and set out for Signal Hill to intercept the enemy force.
In the ensuing Battle of Signal Hill, the player manages to help the defending forces hold the airport and push the attackers back towards the ocean.
Shortly thereafter the defenders receive information about reinforcements being en route to their position.
The group leave a small contingent behind on Signal Hill, and the rest of them decide to continue to push south and out of the city towards San Diego
and the US-Mexico border.
Romeo's team take point in the front of the convoy with Romeo manning the mounted M2 helping engage scattered invading troops along the
highway.
The convoy makes it safely to the LA city limits only to receive a distress signal from the Navy bad at Coronado, about an incoming large amphibious
attack force, requesting the assistance of all nearby US forces. After their final leg of the journey, the troops reach the coast in time to join the battle
of Coronado Island in San Diego, California.


[PDF PAGE BREAK]
(Describe final battle mission)
//.Character note: Romero
His full name is: Ramon Fulgencio Medrano Álvarez
Campaign 2:
Do Right, Fear None
SFC Ferris "Ducky" Ryan
AEGIS Squad - NATO Allied Rapid Reaction Command Europe
In the mission Wirecutter, AEGIS join a team of elite Danish frogmen (team codename Nereid Black) on a nighttime mission to intercept the
Panamanian-registered container ship Sea Lion 7 that they suspect to be a Russian Shadow Fleet vessel running a covert undersea sabotage
operation with the goal of disrupting deep sea internet and communications cable infrastructure in the North Sea.
AEGIS and Nereid execute an amphibious covert infiltration with Nereid infiltrating the Sea Lion from the surface of the sea from a combat craft, and
AEGIS being deployed by helicopter flown by PEGASUS squad onto the ship’s deck via fast roping.
Nereid move to secure the ship's hold while AEGIS head for the ship’s superstructure and the bridge.
The teams encounter unusual resistance from the ship’s crew who are mostly Russian.
After securing the superstructure and several unarmed crewmen that they encounter along the way (those who did not resist the team), and are
contacted by Grim (Nereid Squad Leader) to go into the hold
During a key moment in the mission Nereid discover a concealed compartment at the bottom of the ship’s hold where they happen to interrupt a team
of Vympel FSB Naval Specnaz combat divers (essentially a Russian counterpart to Nereid Black) in preparation for a dive to execute a sabotage
mission.
A firefight breaks out between the Vympel operators and Nereid Black, as AEGIS rush to descend into the hold to provide backup and to prevent a
second team of Specnaz operators also hiding aboard the ship from scuttling it and destroying the evidence.
In an intense close quarters battle in the hold of the ship, the team eventually eliminate all Specnaz aboard and secure the hold.
Grim calls in the status to JCOM (Joint Mission Command), but Lantern points out something’s not right, and suggests to Grim that he and Grim dive
to the undersea cable terminal to check for damage or persistent threats.
Grim agrees, and team Nereid take over the Russians’ diving station and prep for the dive.
JCOM tasks Ducky and his team to protect the upper deck of the ship, while Nereid investigate the underwater terminal, until PEGASUS and TRIDENT
can reach the ship to secure it and airlift AEGIS and Nereid off to base.
In this last part the team then must repel 2 more teams of Specnaz combat divers attempting to approach the vessel in surface attack craft in an
attempt to scuttle it before TRIDENT arrives.
Eventually TRIDENT SIX (DAOG Command ’s codename for the Danish patrol vessel HDMS Freja) rendezvous with the Sea Lion 7, after which AEGIS are
flown off the Freja by PEGASUS TWO (AEGIS Boeing CH-53 Sea Stallion), ending the mission.
Idea for Last Mission: Put in a reference to the Snake Island Heroes ("Russian warship, go fuck yourself!" Spoken by Ducky as he launches the missile
at the Severomorsk) during the oil terminal defense mission where you, playing as Ducky, must fight your way to a Russian-encircled NATO mobile
missile command post, and manually fire an NSM (AGM184A) anti-ship missile from a truck-mounted NMESIS-type launcher, severely damaging the
Russian Baltic Fleet destroyer Severomorsk that is laying down artillery fire on your position from off the coast, holding back reinforcements, and
forcing it to retreat. It is the final part of the final mission in the Game's second campaign in which you play as Ducky from AEGIS Squad fighting to
repel the invasion alongside a detachment of Dutch Royal Marines.
> Attention NATO forces! This is the destroyer Severomorsk of the (Northern) Baltic Fleet of the Navy of the Russian Federation.
You are illegally occupying the Maasvlakte terminal.
Cease fire immediately, and withdraw your forces to allow safe passage for our troops. Acknowledge!
> ...
> Attention NATO forces! If you do not acknowledge and comply, we are going to open fire on your position. You have exactly 1 minute to respond and
comply.
// Ducky arms the NMESIS battery, then reaches for the radio in the command post switches it to the Severomorsk's broadcast frequency, keys the
handset, and says:
> Hey, Russian warship! Go fuck yourself!
// ... and turns the key to initiate the NSM launch
// Missile away!
// On one of the external camera feeds screens Ducky suddenly notices a Specnaz RPG operator pop out of a fucking drain hole net to a pier head
100 yards out and take aim at the command center.
> Aw, fuck! No, no, no, no, no, no, no, no, …
// Ducky scrambles for the command center’s escape hatch as the command center is struck by the RPG, and knocked off its outriggers, tipping over
to the rear, sending Ducky flying against the escape hatch. Ducky manages to pop the escape hatch and emerge from the tipped-over command
center, only to see a plume of black smoke rise from the Severomorsk on the horizon.
The NSM is out of the tube in under 2 seconds, shoots up at a steep angle to about 200 ft, then abruptly levels off and bolts towards the distant ship.
But because the player watches the missile launch he sees a Specnaz operator pop around a barrier about 100 meters ahead of the command post
and fire an RPG at Ducky's position. Ducky attempts to flee but the command post is hit by the RPG and tips over, and he is thrown against the back
of the structure and is forced to pop the escape hatch, emerging largely unscathed, to the ground below. As he recovers, the camera pans out to the


[PDF PAGE BREAK]
sea and over the horizon as the Severomorsk is shown retreating after having sustained major damage to its hull from being struck by the NSM.
Dutch Marine radio chatter that Ducky hears on the air then confirms the ship’s retreat.
Ducky's teammates in AEGIS Squad:
SSGT Aki "Frost" Peltola - former Finnish Special Forces Arctic Warfare Division, now part of AEGIS Squad alongside Ducky. Frost is an elite sniper and
a proficient long-range patrolman and an arctic survival and warfare specialist.
Frost's character is a fictional nod to Siimo "White Death" Häyhä, the famous sniper of the Winter War of 1941. He talks like the mil YouTuber
FalconClaw, who is also Finnish. Wears a mask ísť of the time to hide facial scarring due to old combat injury.
Ştefan “Lupin” Dragavei - former Romanian Army special forces operator. Proficient in assault tactics at range and in close quarters.
LCPL Cassandra Stewart (Callsign: Switchblade)
Originally from Melbourne, Victoria, Australia, she grew up in relative poverty in one of m the suburbs of the city. She lost her mother to an
unexpected cardiac arrest, and her father Richie Stewart became increasingly dysfunctional and increasingly abusive until, one late night, after a long
day of drinking, he fell asleep while smoking on the couch in the living room of their home, causing a house fire. Cassie, 17 at the time was lucky
enough to escape. She confesses at one point in the story that on the night of the fire, she saw her father black-out drunk on the living room couch
among the growing blaze, but feeling bitter and vengeful over the years of abuse she had suffered at his hands, she decided to walk away. After that,
she spent a rough couple months doing mostly petty crime on the streets of Melbourne before deciding to enlist just one week after her eighteenth
birthday.
Campaign 3:
Riptide Red
CPT Trevor "Spook" Gartner
Victor Two Bravo "The Tourists" - CIA Directorate of Operations, Ground Branch
In the Prologue, the Tourists (mission team callsign: Noble; Spook, Tripper, and Smoke; Gartner, Bartlett, and Oakenfold) dispatched by Senior Case
Officer Matthew Mullen (mission callsign: Regent), arrive undercover (as a team of Canadian overland travelers and amateur filmmakers, probably
using film equipment transport cases to take some of the mission gear with them) at Schipol International Airport in Amsterdam. The team pick up a
rental car, Tripper sweeps it for bugs, and they drive to a warehouse near the city's Eastern Docklands area where they are introduced to CIA case
officer Cameron Steele (mission callsign: Emperor) from the Agency's Regional HQ in Frankfurt, Germany. Steele reveals to be working on something
codenamed PANDORA, and is currently working on tracking and investigating a suspicious shipment of restricted networking and communications
technology from Turkmenistan, which is reportedly headed for Atlanta, Georgia, United States. This cargo is currently in transit by train to Vienna,
Austria. Steele then gives the team access to their weapons and the rest of their mission equipment, as well as a mobile operations command vehicle
disguised as an overland RV truck and fitted with the Agency's latest Command and Control technology "courtesy of the friendly guys and gals at the
Frankfurt Logistics Office".
https://www.truckscout24.com/trucks/used/all/tatra
The team are then sent to Vienna to report to CIA case officer Kathy Hughes (mission call sign: Archduke) at the Vienna office located inside the US
embassy building, and receive a briefing on their next objective.

In the mission (mission-name), the team are dispatched to investigate a suspected safehouse used by a Lebanese terrorist cell located at an
apartment building in Vienna's 17th district (Hernals).
Spook and his team manage to enter the apartment undetected, finding it empty, only to be interrupted shortly thereafter by a young woman
returning to the apartment. They hide, but the woman, upon noticing that some of her possessions inside the apartment have been disturbed, she
panics and summons several men from downstairs who show up armed, and begin searching the apartment.
The team try to flee the apartment undetected through a balcony, but are eventually spotted at street level by a group of about seven men in a white
van parked at the apartment building's entrance, who give chase upon contact.
The team run into the courtyard of a nearby large townhouse, hoping to avoid the use of firearms, but are pursued by the men, leading Spook to split
from his two teammates, in the hope of diverting their pursuers.
After a short and intense parkour-style chase, leading the player across the rooftops of Hernals, onto a nearby passenger train platform, and into a
pedestrian underpass, where Tripper and Smoke are able to rendezvous with Spook, after having secured two motorcycles as the team's means of
exfiltration. Spook makes an escape on the backseat of Tripper's motorbike, only for the group to be chased but the van they saw earlier when they
reach the city beltway. A high-speed chase ensure along the beltway, as the men inside the van are revealed to be armed and open fire at the team.
The player, playing as Spook uses a GP SP10A3 STRIBOG PDW (interestingly, the only time you get to use the weapon in any of the game’s story
campaigns, but you can not keep it after the mission) to return fire at the van before the pursuers can hit any of his team, eventually killing the van
driver, and causing the van to careen out of its lane, collide with a concrete roadwork barrier, and explode.
The team finally leave the beltway and reach the Port of Vienna where they ditch the bikes inside a parking garage and are met by two Agency


[PDF PAGE BREAK]
personnel (Junior Case Officers Jerry Hobbes and Daryl O'Brien) posing as city utility company employees, and taken to report back to Hughes at the
Embassy.
At the debrief, Smoke hands in a tablet that the team had recovered from the apartment, and Hughes instructs the team to bring the tablet over to
the Agency tech team at the Frankfurt office, for them to try and extract any useful Intel out of it.
A news broadcast in the background reveals that the fourth-floor safehouse at the Hernals address that the team had previously visited had been
destroyed in a fire allegedly caused by an electrical fault in the apartment's breaker box.
Intel from the laptop contains the mention of Betta Logistics Group GmbH., a sensitive and hazardous cargo logistics company headquartered near
the Frankfurt International Airport, and points to a man named Simenon Christophe Navarre, a French-Canadian-German national and owner of the
company, as the contact for one of the men using the Vienna safehouse where the tablet was recovered. The Intel also seems to mention Karyna
Budanova, Navarre's life partner, and an executive assistant at GenCorp, an international data management company, but provides no further
information on her involvement with the group from Vienna
In the next mission titled Above My Pay Grade set in the outskirts of Frankfurt at nighttime, the team covertly enter Navarre's house and search for
Intel about the shipment. They manage to discover several pieces of paperwork, but nothing enough to go on in their investigation.
Pressed for time, the team decide to locate Navarre inside the house, and move to search the upper floor of the house.
The team eventually confront Navarre in his office. He loses his composure at first, but calms down a moment later, and agrees to give the Player
access to his laptop containing shipping manifests and transaction records.
The Player discovers that the shipment is being prepared for shipping at warehouse 46 in the cargo sector of the Frankfurt airport.
(Information later obtainable by searching Navarre's laptop reveals that the shipment contract is made out in the name of an Israeli defense-orientred
software company called Bastion Infotech, which is ultimately revealed to be a front for a Mossad and CIA black op run as part of the PANDORA plan.
The shipment that the team are tracking down of one of several shipments made through contractors and shell companies from various eastern
counties (but always labeled as coming from a legitimate looking legal entity in an allied European country) into major cities in the United States)
The player can choose to get Navarre and Budanova new identities and a fresh start somewhere far away by calling in a favor with his trusted
contacts back at Langley, at the end of the Navarre House infiltration mission. If the player chooses to help Navarre, Navarre will later in the game call
the player to thank him for what they have done, and to bid them goodbye, as they will no longer be allowed to make contact thereafter.
The team take Navarre's keys, ID, and company van and head to the airport warehouse.
The team arrive at the airport to find the warehouse swarming with Atlas personnel. They pull up to the warehouse side entrance in the Betta Logistics
van and covertly dispatch the three Atlas sentries guarding the door.
They then proceed to clear and secure the warehouse from remaining Atlas personnel, only to find that the shipment had been moved before even
they got there. Tripper manages to extract a hard drive from a destroyed laptop hoping to mine it for Intel later. The team use explosives that smoke is
able to recover from an Atlas armored van on site to destroy the warehouses. It is shown at a later point in the story that in the media, the explosion is
attributed to negligent handling of hazardous substances by the logistics company employees. The news reports never mention any of the entities
involved with the shipment, the presence and involvement of Atlas personnel, or the nature of the shipment previously held at the site.
Upon analyzing the data from the hard drive, Tripper finds mentions of tetherbreak and is able to partially decrypt fragments of messages sent and
received on the laptop proper to its destruction that contain mentions of PANDORA and TETHERBREAK. One message fragment appears to indicate
that the shipping time of the shipment had unexpectedly been expedited following a warning about a possible raid. The decrypted data does not
reveal who the sender of the messages is.
This makes Spook and his men suspect that someone must have warned the Bastion personnel on site about the team's impending arrival in order to
buy them time to covertly divert the shipment to another flight.
Though most of the files associated with PANDORA are corrupted, Tripper manages to recover a partial list of sets of cryptic alphanumeric identifiers
paired with dates and times and what appears to be flight codes that turn out to be untraceable based on accessible Agency records.
Smoke has a hunch that the list might be a shipping schedule of some sort, so Spook decides to call In a favor with a contact at AEGIS, a former
German MAD (military counter-intelligence) officer Karl Alexander “Jaeger” Stanzler, who now works in the PYTHIA counterintelligence detachment
under the DAOG Command , who helps the team match the numbers and dates to a cluster of privately chartered flights that fit the same pattern and
direction as the now missing shipment.
The flight charter contracts are all made out in the names of different US defense supply and security infrastructure contractor companies.
Upon investigating available information about the companies in Agency records, the shipments were declared as containing restricted computer
hardware parts for domestic drone countermeasure applications. The paperwork on file appears to be in order, all the way to the strictest regulatory
requirements.
//At this point, the team should first trace the package back to GenCorp, which leads them to a GENCorp regional head office in Abu Dhabi, UAE.
// The team then travel to Abu Dhabi to raise the GENCorp data center to get the full shipping record of the shipment. This is when the mission
Infrastructure Day takes place. The GENCorp head of Data Security Leandro Blommaert is an optional target during this mission.
// The data they obtain indicates that the shipment was commissioned by a representative of Agarwal Berkhan, an Indonesian-Emirati billionaire
philanthropist and majority GENCorp shareholder.
// The Agency handlers dispatch Victor Two Bravo to Medan City, Indonesia as part of operation DRAGONSLAYER with orders to find and apprehend
Berkhan. This is when the mission Man From Medan takes place.
After the team finish the job at the Medan compound, having failed to capture Berkhan, Spook gets a secure call from Director of Operations at
Langley Robert Macmillan, informing the team that their handler Regent (Mullen) has been “urgently reassigned” to work on a different case, and that
Victor Two Bravo are to report directly to Macmillan (mission callsign: Bishop), effective immediately.
Bishop subsequently assigns the team to a new CIA-NSA joint operation codenamed WHITEOUT, securely uploads new intel for the team that traces
the missing shipment to Miami, FL, and orders the team to travel to Florida and meet with two NSA contacts who are supposed to give them further
information about the case.


[PDF PAGE BREAK]
The team report mission updates back to Emperor at the Frankfurt Field Office, and arrange for a flight back to the US.
They take flight out of Frankfurt to Orlando, FL, and drive to a safehouse in Doral. The Intel they received from Bishop provides additional data on the
shipment's whereabouts. The team head to rendezvous with their contacts, NSA analysts Keith Simmons and Jessica Lynch who can provide them
with the latest operstional updates on the investigation during a meeting at a diner in the nearby town of Medley, FL,
Simmons and Lynch reveal to Spook and his men that they had tracked a suspicious shipment of restricted components from Miami-Dade airport to a
far-right accelerationist domestic terrorist group known as the Kali Yuga Surf Club (based on and visually resembling the real-life white supremacist
Republic of Florida Militia) from Tallahassee, FL, who, only a few hours ago, seem to have moved several large containers of the types used to
transport electronic and communications equipment into the abandoned Desautels Resort Hotel in Miami Beach.
The team drive to Miami Beach to reconnoiter the hotel building, and find that it had been occupied by members of the Los Sites cartel (CLSO).
There appears to be no sign of KYSC at first, but the team surmise that they might be hiding out inside the building. Smoke deploys a thermal drone to
check for heat signatures and identities the possible targets on one of the upper floors of the hotel. The hotel is also overrun with Los Sietes. Tripper
remarks that it is unusual to see a band of wingnut doomsday cultists get a small army of cartel enforcers to run security for them.

leading to the floor below.
Upon reaching the mezzanine lobby, the team are ambushed by a group of 5 elite cartel sicarios. After fatally wounding the last of them, the team
move in on his position only to discover that the last sicario managed to light the fuse to a 2-ton fertilizer bomb that the sicarios have planted it the

before the detonation inevitably levels the hotel.
The team rush to pry open a nearby elevator door and use the elevator cable to slide down to the bottom of the shaft and into the hotel’s
underground parking garage to escape the blast.
The bomb detonates just as the team are reaching the bottom floor of the parking garage, sending the elevator car plummeting after the Player. The
car hits some debris on the way down, becomes wedged inside the shaft, and grinds to a stop before it reaches the bottom of the shaft, saving the
Player from being crushed on impact, and giving them a chance to briefly recover after their somewhat rough landing and pull themselves out of the
shaft and into the floor of the bottom tier of the hotel parking garage.
The team must then fight approximately 15 to 21 cartel enforcers on the way up through three levels of the parking garage before finally reaching an
exit to street level, and exiting about 300ft from the now mostly leveled hotel building, just as first responder vehicles begin to arrive into the scene of
the explosion. The team then quickly slip off to a nearby alleyway and out of sight of any onlookers, ending the mission.

The team discover camera feeds showing vast underground spaces whose existence is completely unknown to them, and according to available
Agency records, it is completely unknown to the authorities and to the public as well. Not even the FBI has documented proof of their existence. The
Agency has, but the knowledge and documentation about it have been unknown to a select few, but not to Spook or any of his trusted contacts. The
facility has existed for decades, since the times of Goldberg's predecessor.

The team must move quietly avoiding detection inside the tunnels. The Player must eliminate enemies stealthily and conceal the bodies to hide them

The player can reach a control room where they can sabotage the CCTV camera feed, effectively disabling the security cameras inside the

The team continue to push further into the underground complex, eventually reaching an apparent dead end in a laundry room, but discover a narrow
vertical shaft with a ladder, accessible through a hidden door inside a small cubby behind a large filing cabinet, and leading to the surface, that they
are able to use to exfiltrate from the compound.
Upon the team's return to the safehouse, Tripper manages to decrypt the extracted data revealing a massive tranche of classified information,

scheme, happening with the full knowledge and active participation of not only multiple domestic federal intelligence and security agencies, but also
the Russia FSB, the Mossad, the IRGC, the Chinese Ministry of State Security, North Korean State Intelligence, pretty much the entire NATO security
apparatus, and several intelligence actors from either nojn-state entities or from geopolitically non-aligned states.

destroy most of the evidence. Ends with Spook and his team being declared rogue by director Macmillan.

Beach Resort at 6701 Collins Ave, Miami Beach, FL 33141 demolished in 2022)) earlier in the story, which the media present as the government

ring, and finally about Riptide Red and the conspiracy at the very highest echelons of the US federal Government involving TETHERBREAK and
PANDORA.

command & control infrastructure and take control of domestic and allied-territory autonomous multi-domain weapons systems and turn them
against the United States. Because if we find a way to do it ourselves first then the enemy cannot surprise us by beating us to the punch.

Why did TETHERBREAK even exist? A glorified penetration test. A compromised rouge clandestine cell?
Well, as one of the collectible pieces of Intel seems to indicate, it was to create a credible threat to covertly motivate and control US mechanisms of
power for purposes of ongoing public civil liberties suppression, and maintaining power. In the words of one of the case officers involved, the
Pentagon thought they were safe with their swarms of ever-vigilant autonomous murder bots. Too safe... TETHERBREAK was meant to keep their egos
in check, so they avoid becoming reckless and breaking the established order, thus threatening the actual (shadow) power structure.
The powerful elite realized that autonomous weapons technology does not put an end to the global power struggle, and having learned from
seemingly superior US technology being bested by comparatively low-tech hacks in the past, they now decided to beat their competition to the
punch by engineering the means of compromising the systems themselves. The idea was to control the black market of exploits aimed against the
technology, to discover and patch any existing vulnerabilities in systems that are already in operation, and last but not least, ensuring that the US
Government won't be able to use the same autonomous weapons systems against the very global elites that the shadow underground represents.
They put themselves in control of the systems, their means of subversion, who gets to access either, and then made themselves immune to the
application of the very same systems against themselves. It was never meant to be used In a terrorist attack, it was an insurance policy, but then
Crodyn’s criminal underworld ties were exposed, then his links to foreign intelligence, then his personal relationship and history of dealings with
Goldberg. Which threatened to expose the whole shadow structure.
That's when the powerful finally caved and went for the nuclear option: stage a false flag attack, topple your own government to stay out of prison,
then start a bunch of wars all over the world, plunge the country into chaos, and then cover your tracks, and keep all the power.
The TETHERBREAK conspiracy seems to be tied all the way up to the sitting US President Barry James Crodyn (pronounced Crow-den, per famous
campaign slogans like "Nobody cares more than Crodyn!"). He also is the owner of the media holding Crodyn Entertainment, and the BJCWorld
modelling talent agency. Also has suspected ties to high-ranking Russian mafia boss Artem Stolyanov (Based on real-life Russian-American mob
patriarch Simeon Mogilevich). Despite being sitting President, most of the time Crodyn resides at the Maravilla estate in Palm Springs, California.
GENCorp (also spelled GenCorp) is the official short form of the name Global Executive Network Corporation - An American multi-national
surveillance data information service and defense Information and communication technology solutions provider with a global market and operations
range.
Indonesian-Emirati billionaire businessman Agarwal Berkhan owns approximately 25 per cent of GenCorp stock making him the largest stockholder at
the time. Barry James Crodyn and Paul Ruetger also own sizable amounts of the company's stock.
Palisade Systems is a US defense contractor with ties to Israel and a listed recipient of "drone countermeasure" technology from Bastion Infotech.
Owned by Paul Ruetger and headed by CEO David Bass. (Obviously Palantír, and CEO Alex Karp)

The exercise that Frost’s unit was taking part in was to be used by Russians as a pretext in public discourse related to the incident, being cited by them
as a means of providing plausibly deniable cover for an illegal incursion of NATO-adjacent forces into Russian territory with intent to carry out
sabotage of Russian military infrastructure. In other words Russia tried to false flag Finnish troops on exercise in Finland, hoping to spin a média
narrative wherein the Finns attacked Russia first, and using the to attack the integrity of NATO, and torpedo public support for European military and
defense policies aimed at protecting western Europe from Russian aggression, framing them as warlike and escalatory.
Kostropov has since that time made it all the way to being Baranov's right-hand man, chief of the Kremlin's intelligence staff and head of the FSB.

Ayatollah Ali Hosseini Khamenei

vibe and less of bumbling fatso manchild compared to his real-life inspiration.
Julien Dufresne - fictionalized Marc Dutroux
Geoffrey-Guy Moffat - fictionalized Jean-Luc Brunel, owner of the GeMo Look International, a high profile Parisian modeling agency.
Spook may be able to confront Goldberg in the very last (?) mission of his story campaign (Sins of Our Fathers), but the player never gets to
apprehend him. The team eventually reach East McFarlane, Goldberg's private West Indian island, discovering massive evidence of Goldberg's human
trafficking and illegal pornography ring, also evidence of cannibalism and ritual human sacrifice within the vast underground complex under the Island.
Spook’s team are determined not to let Goldberg leave the island, and confront him at the helipad of his island property, and find Gillian Stockbridge
preparing to airlift Goldberg off the island. The team appear to have cornered and finally come close to capturing Goldberg, only to be contacted last
minute by Major General Robert Macmillan, the CIA Director of Operations, who says that he had been informed “on good authority” that Victor Two
Bravo (the Tourists) have attempted to go rogue, and orders Spook and his men to stand down and give Goldberg safe passage off the island. This
might be the cliffhanger ending of the first game.

Other DAOG-affiliated allied characters outside of Ducky's Squad:
SSGT Katharine “Valkyrie” Becker - former KSK, joined CORYS squad (peers to their fellow AEGIS operators under the DAOG Command stricture)
after the dissolution of the KSK. Made it to the rank of Staff Sergeant through consistent excellence despite frequent shows of sexism and misogyny
from a loud minority of peers and superiors.
As team leader of CORYS Squad, Katrina's main assignment is protecting the human and physical assets of the AEGIS Command structure (that is,
protection of personnel, and immovable administrative and technical assets)
Though not directly part of Ducky's team, AEGIS and CORYS often operate together, sometimes as parallel teams in a larger squad.
Ilvars "Brick" Kozlovskis - former veteran Latvian SOF, close protection specialist. Part of CORYS squad with Valkyrie.
Riptide Red is the codename of the deep-state conspiracy that planned and executed the PANDORA attacks framed to look outwardly like an act of
war by the People's Republic of China (who, despite possessing intelligence knowledge of KINGMAKER’s existence, are not directly involved in or
seem to know about, Riptide Red). The US’s blaming China for the attack is a plausible pretext for domestic audiences to justify harsher domestic
security policies, suspension of the habeas corpus, and suspension of further us citizens constitutional rights, and at the same time, to destabilize
both the US domestic and the global geopolitical situation and enable the group to carry out an effective coup of the United States, installing Barry
James Crodyn as the 48th president of the US for his unconstitutional 3rd term in office, putting him above accountability for his recently surfaced
criminal history with grievous crimes effectively amounting to treason.
This however sets in motion a chain of events enabling several hostile powers to take advantage of the temporary blackout of US cyber defense and
EW countermeasures to launch a simultaneous amphibious invasion of the US West Coast, for Russia to open a Baltic front in Western Europe, and for
China, who are quick to exploit US weakness, and take this opportunity, to invade and annex the Republic of China in Taiwan.
It is implied that Goldberg may have sold the information about Riptide Red to multiple governments, enabling them to plan out a coordinated
invasion. For those behind Riptide Red, plunging the world into World War Three only served to enhance their odds of escaping accountability, and
realizing their plan to use their wealth to insulate themselves from the consequences of the events that they had set in motion.


[PDF PAGE BREAK]
The Nereid Black Operator characters’ faces are modeled after the slightly age-regressed likenesses of Scandinavian actors Viggo Mortensen (Grim),
Mads Mikkelsen (Rime), Bill Skårsgard (Lantern), and Joel Kinnaman (Undertow). Unfortunately, Nereid Black are not yet available as a playable faction
in-game.
El Cártel de Los Sietes, from Oaxaca, Mexico, and operating in multiple cities across the gulf United States. Their leader is Carlos Miguel Mencia de
Vargas, known by his nickname El Tiburón (The Shark, by his strikingly distinct tattoo depicting a set of skeletal shark jaws that he bears on the
underside of his chin and along the front of his neck) In the game, the player, as Spook, fights numerous Los Sietes members during the mission
Pandora's Box. El Tiburón is not featured as a character in-game as is only mentioned in the mission dossier file, which also includes a photo of him.
The player can also encounter a team of Los Sietes sicarios as Romeo during the mission Down Rodeo. 11 Los Sietes are seen taking cover inside a
street-level bar named the K Lounge (based on the real-life R Bar located at 3331 W 8th St, Los Angeles, CA 90005, USA), exchanging fire with a
25-man detachment of North Korean motorized shock troops positioned in a parking lot partially hidden behind a strip mall section building across
the intersection. These eleven Cartel men are not normally hostile to the Player or his allies, though they will fire back if fired upon by the Player or his
team, or if they spot them trying to enter the bar or approach them past a certain distance.
At this point the player can either choose to:
●​

ignore the engagement and move along, taking advantage of the Los Sietes drawing the DPRK troops’ fire away from the intersection, or
to defeat the North Koreans, after which the Los Sietes retreat, remaining neutral towards the player

●​

circle and flank the North Koreans by taking a back alley route and going down the next street to the south, moving halfway the block,
then take a back alley to the north to emerge in an extremely well covered position in the southeastern corner of the enemy-occupied
parking lot, giving you the upper hand and an opportunity to lay a destructive ambush. After you defeat the North Koreans, the Los Sietes
retreat without becoming hostile.

●​

take out the Los Sites first, and then defeat the remaining North Koreans (quite a difficult fight, since the LS are no joke in combat and
there are 11 of them, and you are also likely to be shot at by the DPRK troops the whole time.)

●​

Wait for one side to win, and then defeat the other, and move along. Again, if the Los Sietes happen to win on their own, they retreat,
ignoring the player, unless previously attacked by them.

Should the Player choose one of the latter two options, they are rewarded by an opportunity to collect another of the game's rare weapons, a CMMG
Mk47 7.62x39mm assault rifle, dropped by one of the cartel sicarios. This weapon is especially useful during the tail end of the first campaign, given
that Russian 7.62 ammo is reasonably often found in enemy vehicles and supply stashes, and dropped by enemies that the player encounters.
The Los Sietes sicarios, on their own, are quite formidable enemies, using elite-level tactics to outmaneuver the player. Though outnumbered in this
encounter, they often are able to hold their own against the enemy shock troops detachment (the battle is not scripted, so it ends up playing out
differently on each playthrough).
The Los Sietes happen to possess 2 vehicles parked outside the bar (a full-size domestic sedan and a 7-seat SUV). If the vehicles are destroyed but
the Los Sietes defeat the shock troops, they retreat on foot through the rear door of the building into the alleyway. If the cars are still in drivable
condition, the Cartel men use either one or both of them to get away. If six out of the eleven sicarios are left, and only the sedan is drivable (with 5
seats), one of the sicarios rides sitting with his legs inside the rear passenger-side side door window of the sedan.
There is another similar SUV that appears to have been destroyed and is stuck burning in the middle of the intersection, indicating that the Los Sietes
may have sought cover inside the bar after the first vehicle of their motorcade got hit and destroyed by North Korean fire.
(Real life MACV-SOG tactic for sabotaging enemy ammunition and ordnance caches: replacing some bullets in an AK magazine with hollowed-out
bullets filled with PETN demolition explosive. This causes catastrophic failure of the ammunition inside the weapon when fired, often severely
wounding or killing the operator. 82mm mortar rounds can be similarly sabotaged to explode inside the mortar tube while being fired)

and breeding programs, the former of which he runs mainly out of the underground facility beneath Montoya Farm. He sees human society as defiled
by weakness manifesting as moralist liberal ideology, and considers its moral and legal standards obsolete and a major hindrance to the powerful
people's true potential for achieving greatness and the betterment of (rich white) men. At his core, Goldberg is just another billionaire with zero
empathy and with a way of thinking largely disconnected from reality, but the role he plays as KINGMAKER makes him much more dangerous than as
if he were just that.

familiar landscape of small town America marred by the jarring symbols of foreign occupation : foreign flags and military insignia, roadblocks and
checkpoints to restrict civilian freedom of movement, uniformed patrols of occupying forces in the streets, ordinary people's lives ground to a
near-halt by the brutality of the experience. It should make the player feel surreal seeing the sight on their own through the Player’s eyes.

// Sequel character.
Vyacheslav “Slava” Timofeevich Glushkin - FSB field officer attached to the occupying force that controls the areas of Calloway and Redbud. He is
seen by the player interviewing Gene Marlow during the second mission Low Ground in Romeo's sequel story campaign Good Morning, America.
Glushkin is likely a major antagonist of Romeo's sequel campaign, and the Player as Romeo gets a chance to kill him during one of his late-campaign
missions in the sequel story. He is a seasoned FSB “illegal”, an agent who had spent extensive time on covert intelligence assignment inside a foreign
country, awaiting to be activated by his handlers at the Kremlin. Glushkin has lived and operated in the US under the falsified FSB cover identity of
aerospace electrical engineer Brent Tibbets from Haverhill, Massachusetts.
Glushkin’s cover persona is extremely convincing. He speaks perfect American English and is well versed in American culture and the realities of
everyday life of Americans. He is not likely to be fooled by most disguises and subterfuge manoeuvres done by the Americans, which is why he is in
the position that he is in at the moment.
His demeanor and style of behavior are heavily based on Christoph Waltz’s character portrayal of the Nazi officer Obersturmbahnführer Landa in the
film Inglorious Basterds by Quentin Tarantino. His looks are completely distinct from Landa’s character, and Glushkin is not a direct callback to Landa,
but is meant to come across as a similar archetype of antagonist. Sophisticated, complex, educated, brilliantly intelligent, charming and
conversationally apt, and well-composed, but hiding a brutally decisive and surgically precise mind with an undeniable killer instinct underneath the
facade.
//Glushkin's full patronymic name is Vyacheslav Timofeevich Glushkin
According to information obtained by the CIA from exfiltrated FSB intelligence records data, Tibbets was born as Vyacheslav Timofeevich Glushkin in
1982 in the city of Volgodonsk, Rostov Oblast, RSFSR, Soviet Union.
Owing to his family’s social status and his father’s Communist Party connections, Glushkin was able to earn a Translation, Linguistics, and
Cross-Cultural Communication degree in English and Mandarin from MGIMO (Moscow State institute of international relations), followed by 18
months of clandestine Linguistics training in English at a covert FSB training facility in Korolyov near Moscow, and then another 18 months of FSB
officer training at the Academy of the Russian Federal Security Service in Moscow.


[PDF PAGE BREAK]
Following the training, he was given the assigned manufactured identity of Brent Henry Tibbets (the stolen or “ghost” identity of a 24 year-old
homeless substance-addicted man without any known living relatives, originally from Haverhill, MA, whose whereabouts have been unaccounted for
since approximately 9 months before the start of Glushkin's deep cover assignment. No one ever reported Tibbets missing, or inquired about his
welfare or whereabouts since his disappearance. There is no official record of Tibbets’s actual remains ever being recovered or identified. There is no
death certificate to his name, and the body is likely still out there, and has either been misidentified as someone else or buried as a John Doe after no
one had come forward to identify or claim his remains. His disappearance from the face of the earth went under the radar of the authorities, which
made Tibbets the perfect cover identity that the FSB needed to plant Glushkin in deep cover inside the United States), and dispatched to the
northeast of the US as an illegal posing as a newly enrolled student at MIT. With the aid of FSB influence and financing, Glushkin earned an admission
to the electrical engineering and aeronautics engineering programs at MIT at age 25, and managed to complete both degrees by age 29. At age 30,
he used the connections he had built at MIT to land an engineering job with Specter Aerospace at the company headquarters located in Peabody,
MA.
Glushkin speaks 9 foreign languages fluently (that’s 10 languages total, if we include his native Russian): English, Mandarin, Arabic, Spanish.
Portuguese, French, Greek, German, and Farsi. He is also well-versed in the history of English, and to a large extent also a history of Chinese
languages, and also has solid knowledge of ancient Greek and Latin. He can also speak conversational level Chechen.
Glushkin is known to semi-competitively play chess, and is proficient at using standard Russian military infantry weapons, owing to his FSB combat
training.

// Sequel note:
China must likely become a major World War Three player in the second game given that with the US cyber capabilities temporarily knocked out it has
effectively become the world's premier digital and military superpower. Not to mention that by annexing Taiwan, China monopolized access to one of
a kind strategic chip foundry facilities
The sequel’s story should show China, having already annexed Taiwan during the tail end of the story of the first game, making moves on territories in
South Asia and the middle east. China is also likely to open a South Pacific Front with NATO by attacking the northeastern coast of Australia. Possible
playable mission in the sequel where you fight a Chinese invasion force off an on the Australian Coast
//Sequel plot note for Ducky's story
At some point the narrative must lead the Player through Ducky's point of view to question who exactly built AEGIS? Who were the architects? Where
did the technology and the funding necessary to build and operate it actually come from?
We know it is supposed to be an “accountable” way of using a fictional EU equivalent of real life palantír software.
And that ties back to the earlier questions. Who made it? European defense companies? Or did the EU buy it? If so, then who from?
These should be the threads that the Player must pull on as the progress on their story.

trapped aboard a ship (or a submarine after, say getting caught by the FSB, and are being taken to a Russian extrajudicial prison. Nereid can pull a
daring assault on the submarine while it is still in port, scuttling it, dealing significant damage to Russian naval capabilities in the Baltics and the North
Sea, and exfiltrating the AEGIS operators to safety in the process).

//SEQUEL PLOT OUTLINE DEVELOPMENT PROMPT:


[PDF PAGE BREAK]
I like the overall architecture of the story that you propose, because it also makes for what I believe to be an exciting change in the play style of the
other two playable characters (Ducky and Spook). The way the threads are interwoven and built has the potential to make the story quite riveting and
to seed some strong threads to lead into the likely 3rd-game storyline (we should not get too deep into the 3rd sequel, IMHO, but soon, we might get
an opportunity after we flesh out what we have already partially built).
Now regarding the significant course-altering campaign event that reaches into all 3 campaign stories, resulting in each campaign's main story
character experiencing this event from a unique perspective, that ties together at the end of the story with the other main character's narrative
perspectives. I have to admit, this is a brilliant plot device that I have also been mulling over introducing, but I have not yet firmly decided on what the
actual event is. I have a few ideas on what this central event could be, I'll tell you mine, and then I'll be keen to hear the suggestion that you mentioned
you have for how this event could be treated in the different characters' campaign storylines.
Here are my rough ideas and suggestions for what the event could be:
●​

Goldberg secretly has a falling out with President Crodyn over matters of deciding what the best damage control is to deal with some
unintended and unexpected developments in the global war that their conspiracy plan just started. Crodyn, having achieved the desired
state of national instability that paved his way to suspending the US election, and being awarded an unconstitutional 3rd term in the Oval
Office as a "wartime president" (As argued by compromised US Supreme Court justices Creighton Howard and Walter Pedilla in their
notes on the SCOTUS's ruling that the two-term presidential limit in office can be temporarily suspended under specific extraordinary
circumstances, such as in the event of a nationwide emergency or an ongoing war on the territory of the contiguous United States), and
after having used vicious jingoistic rhetoric to (falsely) assign blame for the West Coast Pandora attacks on China in the global news
media, framing it in public as an unprovoked act of foreign military aggression aimed against the United States, Crodyn is terrified of the
Russian's strategic pivot towards successful capture and occupation of large swathes of territory of the US east coast. Crodyn, panicking
after the secret deal falls apart, leading Russian President Baranov, North Korean Supreme Leader Kim Yon-Chol, and the Iranian Supreme
Leader Hojjatollah Sayyid Mehrdad Esfandiari to renege on the secretive backroom deals they had previously made with Crodyn's people
in the Riptide Red Circle under the pretext of "going along" with Crodyn's US staged US coup plot (masquerading as a legitimate US
national security response to a Chinese cyberattack) (The topmost intelligence people in Russia, Iran, the DPRK, and in China knew better
at that point than to disturb an enemy who's about to make a fatal mistake), is furious with Goldberg over the failure of the deal, accusing
him of sabotaging the plan to to try to eventually oust Crodyn and hand America right over to its adversaries under the guide of a puppet
government, propped up by people behind KINGMAKER and Riptide Red. Crodyn demands that Goldberg "makes the whole thing go
away" or to otherwise get it back under control by any attainable means. At the height of this private altercation, Crodyn goes as far as to
threaten Goldberg that if he tries to "grow a brain" of his own and seek to throw Crodyn and his political allies under the bus to protect his
ow Status as KINGMAKER, Crodyn will expose him to the public, which for a man in Goldberg's position would effectively be a death
sentence at this point (With his secret role exposed to the public, every intelligence agency and doomsday cult in the world would come
after Goldberg, some for revenge, others seeking to learn what he knows. Others, still, who might seek to overthrow him and take his
place as KINGMAKER, or to simply bring his head on a platter to whoever happens to promise to pay the most for it. Goldberg would
become “radioactive” overnight, ensuring that he is disavowed by his institutional protectors, leaving him exposed and extremely
vulnerable). Faced with an impossible choice and looming betrayal by his likely most powerful co-conspirator, Goldberg resolves to pull a
surprising move: he defies Crodyn’s will and lets himself be apprehended and arraigned in court by US authorities on charges of
mishandling sensitive documents related to the investigation of the KYSC bombing that led to the destruction of the Desautels Resort
Hotel in Miami during the events of the first game. He is given a lenient plea deal by a Florida state prosecutor Lawrence Kaylor
(fictionalized version of former US Florida State Attorney and later Trump cabinet nominee Alex Acosta), and sentenced to a total of 24
months in federal, with earlier parole eligibility no less than 6 months into his sentence, contingent on his behavior at the Coleman Federal
Medium-Security Correctional Facility in Sumterville, FL. A few weeks into Goldberg’s serving out his prison sentence, the Sumterville
penitentiary is attacked by an elite Los Sietes Cartel operations team in a highly-coordinated prison-break operation led by Edgar Murillo
“Bisutrí” Lozada Arias (sometimes also referred to as “El Biz” by some in-game character), El Tiburón’s second- in-command (Arias’s
nickname means “scalpel” in Spanish, an unmistakable hint to the Player about how the Los Sietes’ top sicario is known to operate,
referring simultaneously to the brutality, precision and efficiency of the methods that he chooses to employ in achieving his objectives).
The attack on the prison causes massive damage, leading to the near-complete destruction of one of the facility’s blocks, in the course of
which Goldberg is declared dead, having been killed by the explosion that almost completely destroyed one the prison’s cell block that
Goldberg was held in. It is later revealed that this incident has been a deliberate cover up to conceal Goldberg’s covert extraction by
Bisutri’s team (with the help of Cartel contacts inside the US bureau of prisons, Goldberg and the Los Sietes orchestrate a bait-and-switch
operation planting a mutilated corpse contaminated with Goldberg’s DNA to fabricate evidence of Goldberg’s death during the attack).
The world is convinced that Goldberg is dead, but he has just gone deeper into hiding to recover his resources and launch a clandestine
intelligence “counter-offensive” operation against Crodyn and his circle to reclaim his status as KINGMAKER. I’m thinking Spook might be
able to catch up to Goldberg at this point in his story, prompting an interesting “Dead Man Walking" narrative angle which can, through use
of irony, be relatable to both Spook’s and Goldberg’s current situation at that point in the story. Goldberg being officially dead puts an


[PDF PAGE BREAK]
interesting spin on Spooks narrative, as he is now on a hunt “to kill someone who is already dead”, and knowing full well that the staged
death only serves to put Goldberg ever further out of reach of those seeking to make him accountable for his past transgressions. It is as
if by dying Goldberg has transcended to an even more elusive form of power broker - no longer a mere man, but a kind of false god,
which leads Regent, Spook, and the rest of the Victor Two Bravo team to ask the momentous questions ”How do you kill a god?” echoing
Regent’s words spoken earlier in-game dialogue, and the overall title of Spooks’s campaign’s story. I have no yet decided on the exact
shape of the final climactic confrontation between Spook and Goldberg, but I know we’ve made a rough sketch of that earlier, so later, we
can come back to it and flesh it out when we have crystallized other parts of the story that we must figure out first.​
●​

Another possible suggestion, an alternative main structural campaign event that overlaps in different angles with all three playable
storylines, could be centered around a nuclear strike somewhere in the west. A massive irreversible significant event, with a complicated
background of muddy international geopolitical intrigue. We can choose how we develop this in terms of specific plot points. Will it be
revealed to be yet another distraction perpetrated by Crodyn and his conspirators to lead the public away from the US administration’s
crimes? Is the attack an unplanned consequence of another , yet unknown insurgency or hidden power struggle inside one of the enemy
State powers? Is the attack an escalation to the next phase of the world war? We can choose whichever fits best given the eventual
development of the rest of the story.

●​

The third, but least-developed alternative that I have considered so far is that the momentous overarching event that touches and
influences the story in significant ways could be someone (either one of the player characters directly, or another main story character)
revealing the betrayal of a highly trusted and influential person within either DAOG or some other entity that has heretofore been either
seen as either benevolent, beneficial or neutral towards the players goal. This betrayal reframes this character or entity as hostile and
creates a new sense of pressure, tension and friction that could drive the story in new directions. I don't have any more specific
suggestions to this point yet, but if this proves a viable plot point that we can later develop further, I am happy to revisit and flesh it out
some more.

Out of the three rough ideas that I laid out above, which one do you think makes for the best storytelling development opportunities? AlsoI am now
genuinely curious about the suggestions that you have for what this critical story plot event might be.

//Main character.backstory note: Romeo
Pablo Ignacio “El Furtivo” Hernández Díaz - High ranking Los Sietes-affiliated human trafficker and close business associate of Goldberg 's. Frequently

work with paid-off correctional staff to plant a fake and badly mangled corpse of “Goldberg” with Goldberg's DNA in it in one for the open cells, and
the move to the medical Bay where the bribed guards have brought Goldberg lying on a gurney, covered head-to-toe with a white sheet. Goldberg,
however, is alive and well (the Cartel’s prison staff contacts, having been tipped off about the time of the break, have secured Goldberg in the prison’s

down in for the cartel men to secure the lid and order the COs to take the box out the back of the medical wing and load it into a waiting hearse
(positioned inside the prison facility several hours prior to the breakup by a Cartel team.). They then motion for the COs to drive, while the Cartel men
themselves follow the hearse in their own black SUV. All the while the fighting in the other wing of the prison is still ongoing, mostly among prisoners,
given that El Furtivo and his extraction team are likely already gone by that point. The chaos helps the attackers verte cover their escape and keep she
ckreftik alsecurotu staff busy with riot control and too busy to chat the cartel during their exfiltration
// Second-game character idea:
Yelena “Eli” Dimitrievna Volkova - the real identity of Laura Isabela “La Avispa” Tejada Rojas - a former FSB covert surveillance specialist, who defected
following an operation gone awry, she eventually found her new identity as one of The Los Sietes top people trackers. If you're looking for someone
out there, she’ll find them, typically for a price. She is a high-ranking enforcer and gets her name from her general proficiency at using blades of
various length and types as weapons. But, make no mistake, Laura just as easily knows her way around a firearm and will easily handle anything from a
.22 suppressed pistol to a mounted machinegun, when the situation calls for it.
Appearance-wise, La Avispa is Caucasian with mildly ethnically ambiguous facial features. Her hair is dark and on the shorter side, with a few
occasional faint streaks of grey, parted neatly down the center. Her exact age is not known but she could be in her late 30s, possibly early 40s, as
