PART 4 — SIGNATURE BLADES
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

SWITCHBLADE — Benchmade 3300BK Infidel (OTF automatic)
  3.91" double-edged tanto, matte black DLC. Black aluminum handle worn
  on thumb stud. Finger-hook lanyard mod for draw/retention. Right hip
  horizontal belt clip. Carried since age 17 Melbourne streets — 3rd unit,
  previous two left at scenes not discussed. Origin never discussed.
  Narratively adjacent to house fire beat — never explicitly connected.
  Inspect (Glock 17): left hand visible with forearm scar — no camera
  attention drawn to it.

LUPIN — Romanian Army M1974 bayonet (modified)
  7" fixed, reprofiled/thinned by Romanian bladesmith. Black paracord
  rewrap over original grip panels. Kydex sheath left thigh, edge-in,
  handle forward. Draws LEFT-HANDED. Eastern Bloc steel pattern visible
  to knowledgeable players.

FROST — Peltonen Ranger M95 (Finnish military issue, unmodified)
  Left shoulder strap, handle down. Carried since conscript service.
  Used in Cold Plunge lake encounter — implied, not shown. Handle worn
  smooth. IDENTICAL knife to Lantern (Nereid Black) — acquired from
  Finnish exchange operator. Neither has mentioned this to the other.

CODY BEAUMONT — Buck 110 Folding Hunter
  Stag handle, older style. Father's knife before it was his.
  Right hip belt sheath forward of holster. Recently sharpened —
  keener than anything else on his kit.
  POST-CODY: Appears on resistance cell barn workbench in later mission —
  cleaned, folded, placed deliberately. No scene shows who placed it.
  No character comments. Present the way grief is present.

LA AVISPA — Three-blade system
  Blade 1 (Primary): Extrema Ratio HF3 — 3.5" tanto, partially serrated,
    Forprene handle. 3rd unit — previous two left at scenes not discussed.
    Horizontal belt concealed beneath jacket hem. One-handed draw either side.
  Blade 2 (Secondary/Presence): Boker Magnum Bowie — 12" overall.
    Carried openly on thigh in Los Sietes enforcement contexts ONLY.
    NOT carried with Spook — too conspicuous.
  Blade 3 (Deep concealed): Spyderco Civilian — fully serrated curved blade.
    Appendix inside waistband. Draw-stroke deploys and uses simultaneously.
    Has not used this specific knife. Has used what it replaced, twice.
  PROTECTED LINE: "A gun is a conversation. A knife is a conclusion."
    Spoken to Spook, quiet moment between contacts.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PART 5 — INSPECT WEAPON MECHANIC (finalized)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

BEHAVIOR BY CLASS:
  Rifles/carbines/DMRs/LMGs: Arms-length, rotated slowly right, 3-4 seconds,
    support hand repositions naturally.
  Pistols/compact SMGs: Hand-profile, strong-side. Hammer-check motion for
    weapons with external hammers (CZ P-09, HK45CT, P-99) — varies per weapon.
  Shotguns: Rack-and-check, forend half-inch back and released.

SIGNATURE WEAPON ANIMATIONS: Slightly longer/more detailed.
  Build name in overlay bottom frame for:
  GRAY GHOST / NOTHING / FREYA / TRG M10 / ARGINT / DON'T TREAD
  WREN: NOT in overlay — bolt-open empty-chamber animation ONLY.

OVERLAY (field modification mode):
  Semi-transparent, non-intrusive. Labels near attachment points.
  Empty rails with nothing available: no label shown.
  Field-removable (interactable):
    Suppressors / QD-mount optics / weapon lights / MAWL-DA / MAWL-C1+ /
    foregrips / ammunition type (where multiple types loaded)
  Non-removable (no prompt):
    Fixed barrels / integrated handguards / permanently mounted hardware

AMMO SWITCHING:
  Most weapons: single caliber shown.
  GRAY GHOST: 300BLK SUBSONIC / 300BLK SUPERSONIC — switching requires
    magazine change animation ~4 seconds, NOT skippable. Tactical risk.

PHYSICAL REMOVAL ANIMATION: ~3 seconds. Not skippable.
  Removing a suppressor mid-contact is a deliberate tactical cost.

GRAY GHOST DUST COVER: Faint worn factory marking "300 BLK" visible in
  inspect. Worn from years of handling, not deliberate removal.

MAWL-DA INSPECT (once unlocked on GRAY GHOST): Thumb clicks activation
  dial one position forward and back. IR beam briefly pulses visible.

CLEANING ANIMATIONS (gunsmith between missions):
  Romeo:  Fast, functional, muscle memory. No ceremony.
  Ducky:  Methodical — checks each component before reassembly.
  Spook:  Slow, almost meditative. The cleaning is how he thinks.
  Others: Not yet specified — flag for development.

GUNSMITH SYSTEM (between missions only):
  Laid flat on workbench. All attachment points visible including non-field-
  removable. Categories: Barrel / Muzzle / Optics / Underbarrel /
  Laser/IR / Stock / Grip / Internal (trigger, BCG, buffer — affects
  performance, not visible on model).
  Signature weapons CAN be modified but core identity cannot be changed
  (GRAY GHOST cannot become another color; FREYA color discipline locked).

PART 6 — RARE AND STORY-SPECIFIC WEAPON DROPS
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

CMMG Mk47 Mutant | 7.62x39mm
  Dropped by: K Lounge Sicario Lieutenant (Down Rodeo, Romeo G1)
  Visual ID: Red baseball cap backwards; Crye JPC; shark jaw tattoo on
    right forearm (smaller/black-only — earned but not the full version).
  Behavior: Emerges from side door ~45 sec into contact. Controlled pairs.
    Uses smoke if pinned. More dangerous with Five-seveN at close range
    than Mk47 at medium.
  TIMER: If player doesn't close within ~90 sec of standard sicarios down,
    Lieutenant exits rear door — BOTH weapons lost, NO notification.

Desert Eagle Mk XIX | .50 AE
  Dropped by: Mezzanine ambush leader (Pandora's Box, Spook G1)
  EASTER EGG: First 2-3 sec of Max Payne main theme (solo piano, low
    volume, slightly muffled) plays at EXACT instant weapon settles into
    Spook's hand during pickup animation. Gone before player can process.
    Nothing in game acknowledges it.
  Inspect: Spook turns weapon over once, pauses half-beat longer —
    mildly finding it absurd. No dialogue. Just the pause.

PSS-2 Silent Pistol | 7.62x41mm (4-round cylinder)
  Mechanically unique: completely silent, no muzzle flash, no suppressor.
  Locations: Wirecutter (Vympel officer in hold + Dive Team Commander);
    Burning Daylight (FSB officer stealth section).
  If missed in Wirecutter, Burning Daylight is second opportunity.

OTs-14 Groza | 9x39mm / 40mm UGL
  Locations: Wirecutter (Vympel Dive Team Commander);
    Rotterdam (Spetsnaz demolitions operator).
  9x39mm feeds from AS Val / 9A-91 scavenge throughout rest of mission.

SPP-1M Underwater Pistol + APS Underwater Rifle
  Location: Vympel dive prep station, Sea Lion 7 (Wirecutter, Ducky G1)
  SPP-1M: 4 barrels, dart ammo — silent above water — 4 shots then collectible
  APS: Loaded mag only, functionally useless above water, collectible.
    Ducky's inspect shows visible professional curiosity.

SIG MCX-I (Integrated) prototype | 5.56
  Dropped by: Crimson One, War Wolf (East McFarlane Island, G1)
  Features: Integral suppressor, electronic fire control, round count
    display on receiver visible in inspect. Highest-value pickup on island.

CheyTac M200 Intervention | .408 CheyTac
  Found: Hidden in security post, East McFarlane Island (G1)
  Also: Crimson Two carries personal M200 on ridgeline (different serial).
    Using security post M200 to kill Crimson Two = mechanical symmetry.

SR-3M Vikhr | 9x39mm suppressed
  Locations: Glushkin's close protection (Romeo G2 late);
    KAPITAN (Rotterdam, Ducky); Hull Breach command element (alarm only —
    stealth run = no spawn, no Vikhr).
  Significance: First signal Glushkin has FSB-grade personal security.

MAWL-DA | BE Meyers
  Found: Pelican case, Montoya Farm equipment room (Burning Daylight, Spook)
  Unlock: Tripper opens case, brief cutscene handoff.
  Detail: GenCorp logistics sticker = connects Montoya Farm procurement
    to GenCorp supply chain. No dialogue draws attention to this.

Sako TRG M10 (Frost's backup) | .338 Lapua
  Found: AEGIS equipment cache, Svalbard mission (Cold Frontier, Ducky G1)

PART 7 — NAMED ENEMY WEAPON PROFILES

GLUSHKIN — SR-1 Vektor | 9x21mm
  Civilian shoulder rig under jacket throughout. 9x21mm AP = FSB not
  military. Draws only SR-1 in final confrontation — situation constructed
  to make it sufficient, and he knows it. Holds SR-1 through last words.
  Hammer back, round in chamber — never fired second shot.
  Inspect after death: hammer cocked, round still there. Romeo never fires it.

BISUTRI — HK416 A5 suppressed (primary) + FN Five-seveN engraved (sidearm)
  HK416: Visually identical at distance to NATO SOF kit — character statement
    without dialogue. Purchased through black market military supply chains.
  Five-seveN: Scalpel engraving left slide, "BISUTRI" right slide.
    Not a status symbol — a signature. He had it done himself.
  Fixed blade: Modified surgical scalpel handle with 4" custom blade.
    Nickname is not metaphorical.
  NOT killed in Coleman prison break — Five-seveN only obtainable if
    player defeats him directly in later confrontation.

K LOUNGE SICARIO LIEUTENANT — CMMG Mk47 + FN Five-seveN
  [Full entry above in rare drops section]

WAR WOLVES — Crimson One/Two/Three
  Crimson One: SIG MCX-I prototype + HK45CT (same as Spook's NOTHING —
    implies shared procurement channels, never spoken aloud)
  Crimson Two: CheyTac M200 (personal) + Glock 34 Gen5 MOS long-slide
  Crimson Three: DD Mk18 suppressed + Glock 19 + M67 x2 + flashbang x1
    (first War Wolf to use grenades against player)
  ALL THREE: CFIM-equipped CogniConnect stacks trigger terminal counter-
    forensic detonation on death — rapid ID denied.
    Roman numeral tattoo inside left wrist: I / II / III.
    Visible only during looting animation. Never explained in Game 1.

PART 8 — PER-MISSION WEAPON TABLES (summary of missions developed)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The following missions have full weapon tables developed in thread:
  - Down Rodeo (Romeo G1)
  - Battle of Coronado (Romeo G1)
  - Wirecutter (Ducky G1)
  - Hull Breach (Ducky G1)
  - Vienna Chase (Spook G1)
  - Burning Daylight (Spook G1)
  - Pandora's Box (Spook G1)
  - Rotterdam Finale (Ducky G1)
  - Low Ground (Romeo G2)
  - Dead Air (Romeo G2)

KEY NOTES FROM MISSION TABLES:

DOWN RODEO:
  DPRK + Los Sietes. Romeo starts M4A1 + P320-M17.
  7.62x39mm abundant from DPRK Type 58 + Los Sietes AKM.
  Rooftop cache above K Lounge: Saiga-12 + drum mags + cash (uncollectable).
  DPRK elite squad carries Type 98 (5.56 — NATO ammo bonus) +
    one indigenous bullpup (rare, one mag only, no resupply).

CORONADO:
  DPRK amphibious + Russian Naval Infantry + Iranian IRGC.
  KH-2002 Khara (Iranian 5.56 bullpup) — no dialogue explains why IRGC
    carries NATO caliber. Implies deliberate re-equipping. Just there.
  PKP Pecheneg can be unbolted and carried — movement penalty.
  ORSIS T-5000 on control tower — only G1 appearance.
  Locked cage in secondary hangar: M1014 + nameplate "GUNNERY SGT. R. HARLOW"
    — not a named character; nameplate just a nameplate.

WIRECUTTER:
  FREYA available and primary (first Ducky mission).
  Dive prep station: APS + SPP-1M both present as finds.
  Captain's cabin: Benelli M4 in wall mount + unburned burn bag papers
    (readable intel collectible — routing history of Sea Lion 7).
  Vympel Dive Team Commander: OTs-14 Groza + PSS-2 — emerges partially
    suited from dive station. If player too slow, he may reach the water.
    APS underwater rifle required to follow. Time pressure design.

HULL BREACH:
  Stealth-favored: alarm raised = Spetsnaz spawn = SR-3M available.
    Stealth run = Spetsnaz never appear = SR-3M not obtainable.
  SIGINT room hidden: VSS Vintorez in padded case under console.

VIENNA CHASE:
  Stribog SP10 A3 (10mm AUTO — CONFIRMED CALIBER) + HK45CT only.
  Mission-specific — Stribog cannot be kept. 10mm unusual caliber
    reinforces why it cannot be sustained in the field.
  Chase scenario — scavenging possible but disrupts momentum.

BURNING DAYLIGHT:
  GRAY GHOST + HK45CT. MAWL-DA NOT yet available (pre-unlock mission).
  Supersonic 300BLK mag from Tripper = "break glass" option if mission
    goes loud — acoustic change signals mission character shift.
  Walther P-99 in locked drawer, coat check area — belongs to gala guest.
  PSS-2 second opportunity (if missed in Wirecutter) — tunnel FSB officer.
  MAWL-DA unlock: Pelican case, equipment room, GenCorp sticker.

PANDORA'S BOX:
  Cartel general + elite sicarios + KYSC (5 members, conditioned behavior).
  KYSC fight differently — irregular movement, strange vocalizations, don't
    respond to suppressing fire normally. One already dead on arrival.
  Vector KRISS V (.45 ACP) shares ammo with HK45CT — only exotic pickup
    with sustained utility in this mission.
  Desert Eagle (.50 AE) — 7 rounds total, non-replenishable, Max Payne easter egg.
  Hidden finds: MP5SD in guitar case mount behind bar (pre-cartel occupant);
    Mossberg 590M behind junction box in maintenance corridor (labeled "PETE").

ROTTERDAM FINALE:
  FREYA suppressor-off for first time. Tonal shift deliberate.
  OTs-14 Groza second appearance (Spetsnaz demolitions operator).
  KAPITAN (named kill-feed only) drops SR-3M Vikhr.
  RPG operator: fires from drain hole. Adjacent NATO forces respond
    ~4 seconds after — heard off-screen, not shown. Player who shoots
    him before he fires: RPG goes into harbor, tip caused by shockwave.
    Identical outcome. No dialogue acknowledges player was fast enough.
  Dutch Marine cache in secondary building: Walther P-99 + field notebook
    (readable intel, reveals additional patrol routes on minimap).

LOW GROUND:
  Most resource-constrained mission in Game 2. Romeo's M4A1 running low
    from G1 carry. No 5.56 scavenge available (no enemy uses it).
    Ammo scarcity IS the narrative before any dialogue.
  Glushkin introduction: player observes him interviewing Gene Marlow
    from concealment. Cannot engage. Watching Glushkin operate calmly
    while being unable to do anything = Christoph Waltz archetype landing.
  SR-1 Vektor dropped by close protection IF Romeo breaks cover
    (breaking cover = failed covert observation objective).
  AC-556 handoff from Dale CLOSES the mission — quiet moment before next
    mission's action. "DON'T TREAD" visible in handoff animation.

DEAD AIR:
  AC-556 active and primary for first time. 20-round limit felt immediately.
  Renata Voss carries suppressed Ruger 10/22 — visible in her hands during
    escort. Communicates her situation without dialogue.
  Cody: Mossberg 500 + M&P Shield. Aggressive, reckless, exposes himself.
  Frank Kowalski: AR-15 + Glock 17. Methodical, conservative with ammo.
    One of few allied characters who calls out when running low.
  SVD on water tower: significant detour, worth it.
  Redbud community center cache: unidentified voice on radio gives grid
    reference relevant to next mission. No character comments.

PART 10 — ALLIED CHARACTER PROFILES (weapons development context)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

CODY BEAUMONT (Calloway resistance cell, American Freedom):
  Mossberg 500 Field 28" HUNTING CONFIG — no sling, catches doorframes.
  Mixed 00 buckshot + bird shot (grabbed what was in house — bird shot
  useless vs body armor, players who know will notice, no one says anything).
  S&W M&P Shield 9mm in Uncle Mike's friction-only holster — crimps pouch
  tops before moving so mags don't rattle (worked this out himself).
  Ruger 10/22 .22LR early missions — one scene shows rounds deflecting off
  Russian plate carrier; Cody switches to Mossberg, no comment.
  Vest: Condor MOLLE rig, coyote, road flare (not yet useful).
  Clothing: jeans, flannel, canvas barn coat olive drab — looks like he's
  going to fix a fence. In occupied Calloway, this is camouflage.
  BEHAVIOR: Talks too much in contact, processes in real time, not afraid
  (regulatory absence of fear = what eventually kills him). Last words
  operational not dramatic.
  DEATH: Loading screen showing figure hanged from highway gantry with
  cardboard placard — never confirmed as Cody explicitly. Strategically
  ambiguous. Connection implied, left for player.

LA AVISPA / YELENA VOLKOVA (Los Sietes / Godkiller):
  True identity: Yelena Dimitrievna Volkova, former FSB surveillance specialist.
  Defection route: Venezuela → Cuba → Panama → Mexico → Los Sietes.
  Two firearm configurations:
    LOS SIETES COVER: Ruger LCP II .22LR suppressed (SilencerCo Sparrow) +
      SIG P365 XL 9mm concealed. LCP II in cosmetics bag = relevant on
      occasion. Carries because expects <5 shots total in cover situations.
    ACTIVE OPS (with Spook): HK SP5K 9mm suppressed (SilencerCo Omega 9K),
      Aimpoint Nano, no weapon light (handheld torch support hand instead).
      P365 XL openly in Tier 1 AIWB holster.
  FSB THREAD: Carried PSS-2 during FSB service. Recognizes one immediately
    when encountered with Spook — picks it up, checks cylinder with ten-
    thousand-rounds-worth of economy, fires it at target Spook hasn't ID'd,
    hands it back. No explanation. He doesn't ask. This is the moment player
    understands her FSB background is not distant history.
    [Flag: develop this scene in Godkiller mission writing]
  PHOTOGRAPH: Small folded photo inside jacket left inner pocket. Never shown.
    Spook notices the rectangular outline when jacket moves. Says nothing.
    Predates Venezuela. Story says nothing more.
  ACCENT: Spanish (native-fluent, no accent). Russian (when identity slips).
    English (cultivated ambiguity — not clearly Russian or Spanish).

SSgt ANDRÉ NATHANIEL BRIDGES, USMC (full profile filed separately):
  See character_profile_andre_bridges.txt for complete profile.
  Summary: 28yo, New Orleans Ninth Ward, Black, French Creole name spelling
  deliberate. Enlisted age 20 (2020), E-6 by merit. M27 IAR/ACOG TA31 4x/
  no suppressor, Glock 19M/TLR-7A, OKC-3S bayonet. No weapon names.
  Says "copy" not "roger." Meets Romeo at Port of LA — instant mutual respect.
  Friction = Ranger pushes / Marine consolidates doctrine.
  Signal Hill disagreement outcome TBD narrative thread.
  Calibrated by Coronado. New Orleans/Ninth Ward thematic layer available
  (city that knows what it means to be abandoned by systems meant to protect it).
  Decency as statement in cynical story. [Flag: Signal Hill + Game 2 AFC]

PART 11 — CHARACTER BEHAVIOR / VOICE NOTES (weapons context)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

FROST: Does not comment on enemy weapons. Does not narrate reloads.
  Does not remark on ammo scarcity. One exception: TRG M10 takes a round
  through suppressor — says "Perkele." Quietly. To no one. Transitions
  to MRAD without further comment.
  Cold Plunge final line: in Finnish, unsubitled. Exhausted, deliberate,
  privately furious. Players who speak Finnish understand. Others understand
  the tone.
  Frost/Lupin shorthand: ~40 words total, mix Finnish/Romanian, developed
  at pre-AEGIS joint exercise. Ducky asked once. Frost: "Shooting talk."
  That was the entire explanation.

SWITCHBLADE: Most verbally active in contact. Short specific callouts.
  "Two, left door." "Moving." "Dry — covering."
  Enemy weapon assessment: ~1 second, use or drop. No comment.
  Exception: player picks up AKM in Ducky mission — she glances and says
  "Alright." Flat. Approving.
  Glove modification: removed right-hand finger coverage with scissors,
  week 1 of AEGIS deployment. Trigger feel affected. No permission sought.
  Australian Army patch: left chest pocket, not field-worn, not removed
  despite two requests.

LUPIN: Romanian accent more precisely articulated under stress.
  Sparse/technical weapon dialogue: range calls, wind calls, confirmations.
  No editorializing. On miss: silence ~3 seconds, correction, fire again.
  Unfamiliar weapon handling: systematic personal check pattern — faster than
  formal safety check, more thorough than casual. Same sequence every time.
  Does not do it with his own weapons.
  Data book: Rite in the Rain, written in ROMANIAN. Frost noticed.
  Said nothing. Lupin noticed Frost noticing. Said nothing.

CODY: Talks too much, processes in real time, callouts too long.
  Romeo corrects once. Cody adjusts ~2 minutes, reverts.

ANDRÉ: "Copy" not "roger." Economical in contact. In quiet moments
  asks genuine questions: "How far did you come to get here?"
  New Orleans accent present without performance.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PART 12 — INTER-CHARACTER DYNAMICS FROM WEAPONS CONTEXT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

FROST / LUPIN: Productive complementary pair. Lupin calls range and wind,
  Frost confirms or adjusts. Shorthand unintelligible to others.
  Data book detail + Peltonen knife detail both connect them silently.
  Relationship built on things noticed and not commented on.

SWITCHBLADE / LUPIN: Productive tension. She closes fast, he holds distant.
  She thinks he takes too long. He thinks she closes too fast. Both right
  about the other, wrong about themselves. Never discussed. Just what happens.

FROST / LANTERN (Nereid Black): Share identical Peltonen M95 knife.
  Acquired by Lantern from Finnish exchange operator during joint exercise.
  Neither has acknowledged this to the other.

ROMEO / ANDRÉ: Mutual respect immediate. Friction = professional/doctrinal
  not personal. Rangers push, Marines consolidate. Both legitimately right.
  Best friction type: two competent professionals with different reads.
  Signal Hill: one carries the call, other executes without ego.
  Coronado: calibrated, shorthand established. Relationship has moved.

SPOOK / LA AVISPA: Forced mutual dependence → quiet trust → unique bond.
  Strange romantic tension — fleeting, unnamed, no time to develop.
  Story forces them apart. Perhaps to meet again.
  Her combat control unsettles even Spook (who is himself highly controlled).
  PSS-2 recognition scene = moment player understands her FSB past is present.

NAMED WEAPON BUILDS — MASTER REFERENCE
Fictional FPS Trilogy — Weapons Development Thread
Version 2.1 — Corrected and Complete

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BUILD 01 — GRAY GHOST
Character: CPT Trevor "Spook" Gartner — Signature Primary
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Platform:       Noveske Rifleworks N-4 Gen3
Caliber:        300 Blackout (subsonic primary / supersonic available)
Barrel:         10.5" select fire
Finish:         Solid dark gray Cerakote overall — no markings

ATTACHMENTS:
  Handguard:    NWS-9 M-LOK
  Optic 1:      Aimpoint Micro T-2 1x22 red dot on 0.8" riser (primary)
  Optic 2:      Aimpoint 3x magnifier, swing-to-side mount, behind red dot
  Canted sights:45-degree offset MBUS Pro Offset iron sights (black)
  Laser module: BE Meyers MAWL-DA — player-unlocked after Burning Daylight
  Weapon light: SureFire Scout, M-LOK, extended momentary pressure switch
  Foregrip:     Milled aluminum low-profile angled skeleton grip with
                integrated barrier stop — front-mid underside of handguard
  Suppressor:   SureFire SOCOM556-RC2 (standard)
                [Supersonic mag available from Tripper as break-glass option]

AMMUNITION TYPES (field-swappable via inspect menu):
  300 BLK SUBSONIC   — default; near-silent through suppressor
  300 BLK SUPERSONIC — louder; signals mission has changed character

INSPECT ANIMATION NOTE:
  Dust cover bears a faint, nearly worn-away factory caliber marking
  reading "300 BLK" — worn from years of handling rather than deliberate
  removal. Visible only during the inspect animation.
  MAWL-DA, once unlocked: thumb clicks activation dial one position
  forward and back; IR beam briefly pulses visible in inspect view.

BUILD NAME displayed in inspect overlay: GRAY GHOST

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BUILD 02 — NOTHING
Character: CPT Trevor "Spook" Gartner — Signature Sidearm
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Platform:       HK45CT
Caliber:        .45 ACP
Finish:         Dark gray Cerakote — matches GRAY GHOST

ATTACHMENTS:
  Weapon light: Streamlight TLR-7A
  Suppressor:   Nielsen device suppressor (fitted)

NARRATIVE NOTE:
  Name functions as both weapon identity and operational cover — when
  asked what he is carrying, Spook's answer "Nothing" is technically,
  literally true. Delivered completely flat. No smile. No pause.
  Works as a recurring thread across Godkiller missions — used sparingly;
  lands differently each time as the player accumulates context.
  First use: almost funny. Second: unsettling. Third: the word itself
  carries weight.
  [Flag for Godkiller mission dialogue development — main narrative thread]

BUILD NAME displayed in inspect overlay: NOTHING

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BUILD 03 — FREYA
Character: SFC Ferris "Ducky" Ryan — Signature Primary
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Platform:       Grand Power R-15 Freya GEN 2
                (fictional 2nd-gen prototype of the real Grand Power R-15)
Caliber:        5.56x45mm NATO
Barrel:         16" cold hammer-forged match-grade

GEN 2 PROTOTYPE SPECIFICS:
  - No forward assist
  - No magwell ports (clean, uninterrupted lower profile)
  - Ambidextrous bolt release (GEN 2 refinement)
  - Refined trigger group developed from AEGIS operator feedback
  - Weapon card flavor text: "Pre-production evaluation unit, serial 004 of 12"

COLOR SCHEME:
  Receiver / upper / lower / handguard:   Olive green
  Barrel / buffer tube / muzzle device:   Black
  Pistol grip / stock:                    Black
  Optic 1 housing (Aimpoint Comp M5s):    FDE
  Magnifier housing:                      FDE
  Canted sights / QD sling D-ring /
  small hardware:                         Black

ATTACHMENTS:
  Rail:         Geissele MK4 M-LOK
  Optic:        Aimpoint Comp M5s on 1.5" riser — FDE housing
  Laser module: MAWL-C1+ (AEGIS standard)
  Weapon light: SureFire Scout Pro, M-LOK at 9 o'clock
  Grip:         Magpul MOE-K2 (black)
  Stock:        BCM Gunfighter (black)
  Suppressor:   B&T Rotex-V (available; removed for Rotterdam finale)

INSPECT ANIMATION NOTE:
  Suppressor-off config first appears in Rotterdam finale — sounds and
  handles noticeably differently from suppressed config; deliberate
  tonal shift from AEGIS standard operational register.

BUILD NAME displayed in inspect overlay: FREYA

BUILD 05 — DON'T TREAD
Character: LT Ramón "Romeo" Álvarez — Early Game 2 Primary
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Platform:       Ruger AC-556 (military selective-fire variant)
Caliber:        5.56x45mm NATO
Config:         Folding stock, compact tactical variant
Magazines:      20-round factory magazines

PROVENANCE:
  Given to Romeo by Dale Pruett at the end of mission Low Ground.
  Dale retrieved it from a locked gun safe in his barn.
  Handoff animation: unhurried — Dale checks action, wipes receiver
  with a cloth, passes it stock-first to Romeo.

ENGRAVING:
  Left side of receiver — small eagle clutching a banner reading:
  "DON'T TREAD"
  Spelled exactly as it appears on the Gadsden flag.
  Appears to have been done by hand, possibly with a Dremel,
  at some point in the weapon's past.

ENVIRONMENTAL ECHO:
  A detail in Dale's house — framed photograph or jacket patch —
  echoes the same truncated motto, tying Dale to the weapon's origin
  without any dialogue drawing attention to it.

NARRATIVE FUNCTION:
  Early-campaign primary only. 20-round magazine limit and moderate
  accuracy ceiling mean the player naturally phases it out as better
  options become available — making the moment of setting it aside
  a quiet story beat in itself.

STORY FLAG:
  In Act Two, a member of the Three Percenter / Boogaloo-adjacent
  militia group recognizes the engraving when Romeo is carrying
  DON'T TREAD — creating a moment of dangerous mistaken assumption
  Romeo must navigate carefully.
  [Full development reserved for main narrative thread]

INSPECT ANIMATION NOTE:
  The "DON'T TREAD" engraving is clearly visible during the inspect
  animation. No character draws attention to it.

BUILD NAME displayed in inspect overlay: DON'T TREAD

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BUILD 06 — TRG M10
Character: SSGT Aki "Frost" Peltola — Signature Primary
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Platform:       Sako TRG M10
Caliber:        .338 Lapua Magnum
Barrel:         27" fluted match-grade, threaded muzzle
Finish:         Chassis — olive drab
                Barrel and suppressor — matte black
                Scope body — matte black
                Scope caps — tan (always closed when not in use)

ATTACHMENTS:
  Suppressor:   Sako / Vaime SAR .338 (Finnish-made; run as permanent
                fixture in field conditions)
  Optic:        Schmidt & Bender PM II 5-25x56
                (reticle worn at center from years of use; tracking exact)
  Bipod:        Atlas BT10 V8 on ARCA rail at forend
  Magazine:     5-round detachable box; 6 spare magazines in dedicated
                chest pouch
  Ammunition:   Lapua Scenar 250gr BTHP
                (hand-loaded in garrison; factory Lapua in field)
  Stock:        Adjustable LOP and cheek piece height; both set to Frost's
                exact measurements; marked with small white ink lines for
                return-to-zero after transport

NAME NOTE:
  The TRG M10 is not a name Frost gave the weapon. It is simply what
  the weapon is — the platform name and the build name are the same
  because the weapon and the man are so closely identified that the
  distinction ceased to matter. Frost does not name his weapons.
  The TRG M10 is just what it is, and everyone who knows Frost
  knows what that means.

BUILD NAME displayed in inspect overlay: TRG M10

INSPECT ANIMATION NOTE:
  Frost rotates rifle slowly; runs right thumb along bolt handle
  (habitual checking motion); checks suppressor lockup with two fingers
  (quarter-turn test); does not open bolt; scope caps remain closed
  throughout. The rifle is always ready but never presumptuous about it.

BUILD 07 — [FROST'S COLD PLUNGE RIFLE — MISSION SPECIFIC]
Character: SSGT Aki "Frost" Peltola — Cold Frontier 07 flashback only
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Platform:       Tikka T3x TAC A1
Caliber:        .308 Winchester
Config:         Standard Finnish military exercise configuration
Optic:          Kahles K624i in standard military mount
Finish:         Factory synthetic stock, utilitarian

NARRATIVE NOTE:
  Carried by young Frost during Cold Frontier 07 exercise in Lapland.
  Lost when Frost goes over the cliff into the icy lake — knocked from
  his hands during the fall. Not recovered. Not available as a pickup.
  Its loss is the narrative origin of Frost's preference for distance.
  He learned in that lake what happens when distance fails.

BUILD 08 — WREN
Character: LCPL Cassandra "Switchblade" Stewart — Signature Primary
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Platform:       Steyr AUG A3
Caliber:        5.56x45mm NATO
Finish:         Olive green (factory — darker shade than FREYA;
                closer to Australian AUSCAM green than European NATO green)
                Present since her Australian Army service; never repainted
                by AEGIS.

ATTACHMENTS:
  Rail:         NATO standard Picatinny top rail
                (replacing AUG factory optical system)
  Optic:        Trijicon MRO red dot on 1.5" absolute co-witness mount
  Laser module: MAWL-C1+ at 12 o'clock forward position (AEGIS standard)
  Weapon light: Modlite OKW, M-LOK side mount at 9 o'clock
  Suppressor:   SureFire SOCOM556-Mini2 (compact; run suppressed on most
                operations; removed when psychological effect of unsuppressed
                report is tactically useful)
  Grip:         AUG factory thumbhole stock grip — unchanged
  Sling:        Blue Force Gear Vickers VCAS — single-point converted
                to two-point

BUILD NAME NOTE:
  "WREN" — written in black marker on the inside of the dust cover.
  Not visible during normal gameplay. Only readable during the
  bolt-open animation after the last round, when the dust cover is
  briefly visible. Switchblade has never told anyone the name.

INSPECT ANIMATION NOTE:
  Build name NOT displayed in inspect overlay — unlike FREYA, GRAY GHOST,
  ARGINT, TRG M10, NOTHING, and DON'T TREAD.
  WREN is discoverable only via the bolt-open empty-chamber animation.
  A detail exclusively for attentive players.

BUILD 09 — ARGINT
Character: CPL Ştefan "Lupin" Dragavei — Signature Primary
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Platform:       FN SCAR-H DMR configuration
Caliber:        7.62x51mm NATO
Barrel:         20" DMR barrel
Finish:         Factory flat dark earth
                [Field adaptation: strip of black electrical tape along
                top of suppressor body to reduce heat shimmer visible
                through optic at sustained fire — documented by AEGIS
                armorer as "field adaptation, non-structural"]

ATTACHMENTS:
  Trigger:      Geissele Super SCAR (precision trigger group)
  Optic:        Nightforce NX8 1-8x F1 (first focal plane LPVO)
  Backup optic: Trijicon RMR, offset at 45 degrees for CQB transitions
  Laser module: MAWL-C1+ at 12 o'clock
  Weapon light: SureFire Scout Pro at 9 o'clock M-LOK
  Bipod:        Atlas BT10 V8 (same as Frost and Lantern)
  Grip:         Magpul MOE-K2
  Stock:        Factory SCAR-H folding stock — maximum length of pull
  Suppressor:   SureFire SOCOM762-Mini2

BUILD NAME NOTE:
  "ARGINT" — Romanian for silver. Written in small block letters on
  the underside of the stock in black marker. Silver because the round
  is large and old and reliable, and Lupin respects all three qualities.
  He did not explain the name to anyone. Frost read it once during a
  weapons inspection, said nothing, and that was the end of it.

BUILD NAME displayed in inspect overlay: ARGINT

SWITCHBLADE — Benchmade 3300BK Infidel (OTF automatic)
  Blade:        3.91" double-edged tanto profile, matte black DLC coating
  Handle:       Black aluminum, worn on thumb stud from repeated deployment
  Modification: Lanyard hole with split ring for simultaneous
                finger-hook deployment and retention
  Carry:        Right hip, horizontal belt clip
  History:      Carried since age 17, Melbourne streets; upgraded twice
                since then; origin not discussed; narratively adjacent
                to the house fire story beat — never explicitly connected

LUPIN — Romanian Army M1974 bayonet (modified)
  Blade:        7" fixed; profile thinned and reprofiled by Romanian
                bladesmith; tip reground to fine point from original
                bayonet geometry
  Handle:       Re-wrapped in black paracord over original grip panels
  Sheath:       Kydex, left thigh, edge-in, handle forward
  Draw:         Left-handed
  Provenance:   Romanian Army issue; steel shows Eastern Bloc manufacture
                pattern recognizable to Warsaw Pact-familiar players

FROST — Peltonen Ranger M95 (Finnish military issue, unmodified)
  Carry:        Left shoulder strap, handle down
  History:      Carried since Finnish conscript service; used in Cold
                Plunge lake encounter (implied, not shown on screen);
                handle worn smooth at grip point from years of carry
  Shared note:  Lantern (Nereid Black) carries an identical knife —
                acquired from a Finnish exchange operator; connects
                Frost and Lantern without requiring a scene about it

CODY BEAUMONT — Buck 110 Folding Hunter (lockback folder)
  Handle:       Stag — older style
  Provenance:   His father's knife before it was his
  Carry:        Belt sheath, right hip, forward of Shield holster
  Edge:         Recently sharpened — keener than the rest of his kit
  Post-Cody:    Found on resistance cell barn workbench in a later mission;
                cleaned, folded, placed there deliberately;
                no scene shows who placed it there;
                no character comments on it

LA AVISPA — Three-blade system

  Blade 1 (Primary):
    Extrema Ratio HF3 (fixed blade)
    3.5" partially serrated, tanto tip, Forprene handle
    Third unit — previous two left at scenes not discussed
    Carry: horizontal belt position, concealed beneath jacket hem
    Draw: one-handed from either side

  Blade 2 (Secondary / Presence weapon):
    Boker Magnum Bowie (12" overall)
    Carried openly on thigh in Los Sietes enforcement contexts
    NOT carried when operating with Spook — too conspicuous
    Drawn slowly in enforcement contexts; the assessment has already
    been made before the draw begins

  Blade 3 (Deep concealed):
    Spyderco Civilian (fully serrated curved blade)
    Appendix inside waistband under any garment
    Designed for draw-stroke deployment — single motion deploys
    and uses simultaneously
    Has not used this specific knife;
    has used what it replaced, twice

  Signature line (spoken to Spook, quiet moment between contacts):
  "A gun is a conversation. A knife is a conclusion."

================================================================================
INSPECT WEAPON MECHANIC — DESIGN REFERENCE
================================================================================

BEHAVIOR BY WEAPON CLASS:

  Rifles / carbines / DMRs / LMGs:
    Arms-length presentation; weapon pulled slightly back and rotated
    slowly to the right; three-quarter view of receiver, optics,
    handguard; approximately 3-4 seconds full inspect; support hand
    repositions naturally to allow the view

  Pistols / compact SMGs:
    Weapon raised slightly and turned to strong-side profile;
    for weapons with visible hammers (CZ P-09, HK45CT, P-99)
    animation includes a brief hammer or safety check motion —
    one mechanical gesture that varies per weapon

  Shotguns:
    Short rack-and-check motion; forend pulled back a half-inch
    and released; functional rather than aesthetic

SIGNATURE WEAPON EXTENDED INSPECT:
  Signature builds receive slightly longer or more detailed animations
  Build name appears in small text at bottom of inspect frame for:
  GRAY GHOST / NOTHING / FREYA / TRG M10 / ARGINT / DON'T TREAD
  WREN does not appear in overlay — discoverable only via
  bolt-open empty-chamber animation

OVERLAY SYSTEM (field modification mode):
  Semi-transparent non-intrusive overlay during inspect
  Labels appear near attachment points with available interactions
  Empty rails with nothing available show no label
  Field-removable attachments interactable during inspect:
    — Suppressors (threaded barrels)
    — Optics on quick-detach mounts
    — Weapon lights (M-LOK / Picatinny)
    — MAWL-DA and MAWL-C1+ laser modules
    — Foregrips (M-LOK / Picatinny)
    — Ammunition type where multiple types carried
  Non-removable in field (no prompt appears):
    — Fixed barrels
    — Integrated handguards
    — Permanently mounted hardware

AMMUNITION SWITCHING (inspect menu):
  Most weapons: single caliber option shown
  GRAY GHOST: 300 BLK SUBSONIC / 300 BLK SUPERSONIC
    Switching requires magazine change animation — approximately
    4 seconds; not skippable; tactical risk if done mid-contact

REMOVAL ANIMATIONS:
  Physical attachment removal: approximately 3 seconds
  Not skippable — removing a suppressor mid-firefight is a
  deliberate tactical decision with real time cost

CHARACTER-SPECIFIC CLEANING ANIMATIONS (gunsmith):
  Romeo:  Fast and functional; muscle memory; no ceremony
  Ducky:  Methodical; checks each component before reassembly
  Spook:  Slow and almost meditative — the cleaning is something
          he does when he needs to think

END OF NAMED WEAPON BUILDS — MASTER REFERENCE
Version 2.1 — Corrected and Complete

PROJECT WARRIORS — EPIC AIRCRAFT & VEHICLE SCENE TREATMENTS
Master Document — All Seven Scenes
Compiled from Meta Thread and Sidebar Development
========================================================

DOCUMENT STATUS KEY:
[FULL TREATMENT] = Complete narrative scene with full dialogue written
[CONCEPT + PARTIAL] = Narrative concept developed, some dialogue, placement TBD
[CONCEPT ONLY] = Idea established, needs dedicated development session

========================================================


SCENE 1 — THE GRIPEN FLYOVER [FULL TREATMENT]
Aircraft: JAS 39 Gripen (x2) — PHAETON Flight, Swedish Air Force
DAOG Designation: PHAETON
Campaign: Persistent Threat (Ducky) — Game 2
Placement: TBD — tentatively Hard Winter or Dead Frequency

--------

CONCEPT

A world-scale moment embedded in a ground-level mission. The player — as Ducky — exits dense forest or terrain cover and enters a clearing with open sky. Swedish Air Force Gripens pass in a low fast attack run, deploying into a break maneuver after the pass. The scene establishes that AEGIS is operating inside something much larger than a four-person squad, and briefly makes the squad feel small inside something vast — before contracting back to ground level. Frost's single line afterward is the scene's emotional punctuation.

AUDIO ARCHITECTURE — THREE PHASES

Phase One — The Frequency: Radio chatter begins as ambient background — not directed at the player, not requiring response. In Swedish. The player who doesn't speak Swedish hears cadence and register — professional, clipped, military aviation communication rhythm — without understanding content. This is intentional. A brief exchange in English on DAOG liaison frequency establishes position and intent:

"AEGIS element, this is PHAETON flight, two Gripens, we have you visual. Ten clicks northeast, maintaining altitude. Standing by for tasking."

Ducky responds briefly — confirms position, acknowledges support. Radio returns to Swedish between the two aircraft.

Phase Two — The Approach: Squad continues moving. Forest thins. Sound design begins its work — jet noise building from a hum that could be wind, to a frequency the player's body registers before their ears consciously identify it, to something unmistakably mechanical and fast and getting faster. Directionality shifts — behind, above, closing. The clearing opens. The sky appears. Player has full control throughout.

Phase Three — The Exposure: Gripens come in low and fast from behind the player's position. Sound arrives before the aircraft — engine noise reaches full intensity in the half-second before jets cross the player's field of view. They are overhead and gone in under three seconds. The player who was looking at the right part of the sky catches them fully. The player who was looking elsewhere catches the blur, the shadow, the physical pressure of the sound.

CAMERA NOTE

A dynamic camera pull mimics the involuntary response of a trained person to fast-moving aircraft overhead. Not taking control away from the player — nudging the camera upward with just enough force that looking up feels like something their character did rather than something the game did to them. If it feels like the game is making them look, it breaks immersion. If it feels like Ducky's head just moved, it deepens it.

POST-PASS

Gripens peel off after the pass — one banking left, one banking right. The specific visual of a two-ship breaking into separate egress vectors. Afterburner catch in the light if the time of day supports it. Then gone, climbing, sound receding as fast as it arrived.

"AEGIS, PHAETON flight departing for tasking. Good hunting."

Then Swedish again between the two pilots — briefly, something that sounds like it might be humor. The specific register of two people in high-performance aircraft who are very good at what they do and know it. Then silence. The forest. The squad. The scale contracting back to four people on the ground.

FROST'S LINE

After a moment:

"Finnish Air Force flies Hornets."

Nobody asks why he said that. Nobody needs to.

THEMATIC FUNCTION

The scene expands the player's perceptual world from squad-sized to theater-sized, then contracts it back. The contraction is as important as the expansion — the contrast produces the feeling. The player feels small after the Gripens peel off. But small in the specific way of someone who is part of something large, not the small of someone who is alone. The radio chatter in Swedish communicates that the world does not exist to serve the player's comprehension of it. Allied forces speak to each other in their own languages. The war has its own life outside the missions.


========================================================


SCENE 2 — THE A400M PASSAGE [FULL TREATMENT]
Aircraft: Airbus A400M Atlas — ICARUS Flight, Belgian Air Component / DAOG
DAOG Designation: ICARUS
Campaign: Persistent Threat (Ducky) — Game 2
Placement: TBD — tentatively Permafrost (Svalbard approach) or Cold Open withdrawal

--------

CONCEPT

Where the Gripen scene is fast, kinetic, gone before the player fully processes it — the A400M passage is slow. Enormous. Impossible to ignore and impossible to hurry. The A400M is one of the largest military transport aircraft currently in service. Its four turboprop engines produce a sound completely unlike jet noise — lower, more pervasive, with a physical quality that fighter jets do not have. You hear an A400M coming for a long time before you see it, and continue to hear it for a long time after it is gone. This is the scene's entire mechanism. Length. Duration. The aircraft taking an unreasonable amount of time to cross the sky, and the player unable to look away.

SETUP — THE ANTICIPATED ARRIVAL

Unlike the Gripen scene — which catches the player mid-movement with no warning — the A400M scene is partially anticipated. Radio chatter establishes it coming. Communication switches between French and Dutch and English in the specific way of a Belgian military crew — Belgium's linguistic division means Belgian military units routinely operate in both national languages plus English as a working lingua franca.

"AEGIS, ICARUS Zeven, A400M, we are inbound your position, carrying medical and ammunition resupply, ETA twelve minutes."

Then French between crew members. Then Dutch. Then English again for DAOG coordination. The player has twelve minutes of game time — compressed, but felt — before the aircraft arrives. Long enough to continue the mission's current activity. Long enough to almost forget the inbound call. Long enough that when the sound begins it arrives as something half-expected and still surprising.

THE ARRIVAL

The A400M comes in low — lower than it should be for a transport aircraft, low enough that the player who looks up sees detail. The four propeller discs catching the light. The massive fuselage with ICARUS wing markings and Belgian Air Component roundels. The specific silhouette of an aircraft that is all utility, all capacity, no elegance — and beautiful for being exactly what it is rather than anything more.

It crosses the sky slowly enough that the player can watch the whole passage. No sudden peel-off, no afterburner flash. It simply continues, enormous and unhurried, the engine sound filling everything and then gradually, over thirty seconds, vacating it. The sky after an A400M passage feels emptier than the sky before it.

RADIO — POST-PASS

The ICARUS crew confirming drop zone approach. French between the loadmaster and the pilot. The sound of the cargo ramp opening transmitted accidentally on the coordination frequency — a brief burst of wind noise and crew voices from inside the aircraft — before the channel clears.

Then, from somewhere below the flight path, a ground element that isn't AEGIS — unidentified, whose presence the player only infers from this exchange:

"ICARUS Zeven, confirmed. Come around for second pass, we have a marking panel on the north end."

The A400M banks. Begins its circuit. It will be back. The player's squad continues their mission. The aircraft continues its work. Two operations, parallel, neither aware of the other's full picture. The war being large enough to contain both simultaneously.

THEMATIC FUNCTION

The A400M is carrying something toward the place the squad is trying to protect. The supply and the protection are different expressions of the same purpose. The scene does the same tonal work as the Gripen scene — expanding then contracting the player's sense of scale — but at a completely different speed and register. The Gripen scene is a three-second shock. The A400M passage is a thirty-second weight.

SVALBARD PLACEMENT NOTE

If placed during the Permafrost mission's approach phase: the A400M coming in over the fjord, enormous against the grey Norwegian sky, before the squad descends into the mission. The aircraft is carrying something toward the AEGIS datacenter that the squad is trying to protect — supply and protection as parallel expressions of the same purpose. The player who watches it cross the Svalbard sky before the mission begins understands AEGIS as an institution rather than just a squad.


========================================================


SCENE 3 — THE A-10 ATTACK RUN [CONCEPT ONLY — NEEDS DEVELOPMENT]
Aircraft: A-10 Thunderbolt II
Campaign: Romeo — Game 3
Location: American suburban environment (specific location TBD)

--------

CONCEPT (summary only — full scene not yet written)

An A-10 Warthog makes a low attack run over or near a recognizably American suburban neighborhood. The image of the aircraft — its distinctive silhouette and the unmistakable sound of the GAU-8 Avenger cannon — against the backdrop of ordinary American houses, yards, and streets. The contrast between the domestic scale of the landscape and the violence of the aircraft is the emotional payload.

The A-10 is chosen deliberately for its iconic visual identity — no aircraft in the US inventory is more immediately recognizable by silhouette — and for its sound signature, which is unlike any other aircraft in service. The GAU-8 cannon sound (the famous "BRRRT") carries enormous cultural recognition among the gaming audience and would land with immediate visceral impact.

STATUS: CONCEPT ONLY. Specific mission, location, dialogue, and narrative mechanic all TBD.
NEEDS: Dedicated development session to write the full scene.


========================================================


SCENE 4 — THE RED DAWN CALLBACK — PARATROOPER DROP [CONCEPT + PARTIAL]
Location: Smoky Mountains, visible from distance
Campaign: American Freedom (Romeo) — Game 2
Placement: Navigation moment in a mission, specific mission TBD

--------

CONCEPT

At a specific point during Romeo's American Freedom campaign, the player — while navigating on foot through terrain — spots in the distance over the Smoky Mountains a formation of enemy paratroopers descending. The parachutes are visible at distance — a deliberate callback to the 1984 film Red Dawn.

DUAL NARRATIVE PURPOSE

1. In-world navigation device — the player sees where the paratroopers are landing and understands instinctively that this is where the mission is heading. No radio prompt, no waypoint, no UI element. The world tells the player where to go.

2. Deliberate visual homage to Red Dawn — designed to be felt rather than stated. No dialogue draws attention to it. The reference should never be made explicit in any in-game element.

DIALOGUE

Minimal by design — this is largely a wordless cinematic moment. Any dialogue that exists around it should be understated and not draw attention to what the player is seeing. A teammate noticing the chutes. A brief, flat acknowledgment. Nothing more.

TRAILER / PROMOTIONAL NOTE

Flagged as strong standalone trailer asset. Suggested treatment: shot opens on the Smoky Mountains peaceful and still in early morning. Then paratroopers begin to appear — first one, then dozens. Music shift completes the moment. The image works for players who know Red Dawn and works independently as a striking image for those who don't.

STATUS: CONCEPT AND NARRATIVE MECHANICS DEVELOPED. Full dialogue minimal by design and TBD. Needs short development session to finalize any dialogue around the moment and confirm mission placement.


========================================================


SCENE 5 — THE KERAUNOS URBAN PRECISION STRIKE [FULL TREATMENT]
Aircraft: Dassault Rafale B (x2) — KERAUNOS Flight, French Air and Space Force
DAOG Designation: KERAUNOS
Weapons: AASM Hammer precision air-to-ground munitions
Campaign: Persistent Threat (Ducky) — Game 2
Location: Urban / built-up environment in Western Europe (specific city TBD)

--------

CONTEXT AND NARRATIVE SETUP

Ducky and AEGIS Squad are pinned down by a fortified Russian or enemy position in a dense urban environment — a reinforced building, a blocked street corridor, a bridge approach, or a key infrastructure chokepoint. Too heavily defended for AEGIS to take by direct assault. Ducky or Lt. Tara Halliday (ORACLE) calls in the strike through DAOG Command channels. Colonel Mark Walker (ARES) approves. KERAUNOS FLIGHT acknowledges and begins their attack run. The player, as Ducky, is ordered to pull back to a safe observation distance and hold.

THE STRIKE SEQUENCE — FULL SCENE

[The squad takes cover behind a low wall or in a doorway with a clear line of sight to the target building approximately 200-300 metres ahead. The street between them and the target is empty — rubble, abandoned vehicles, broken glass. It is quiet for a moment, the kind of quiet that precedes something.]

DUCKY:
(into radio, clipped and dry)
KERAUNOS FLIGHT, this is AEGIS ACTUAL. Target is marked. You are clear hot. How copy?

KERAUNOS LEAD:
(French-accented English, calm and professional, slight static on the radio)
AEGIS ACTUAL, KERAUNOS LEAD. Copy clear hot. Tally the mark. Running in now. Stand by.

[A beat. Silence. Then — heard before seen — a rising, tearing sound from the west. High and fast. Both Rafales come in low and fast over the rooftops, in close formation, wings loaded with AASM Hammer munitions, the Thales Damoclès targeting pods visible under the fuselage. They are moving at speed — not the slow, gravitational presence of the AC-130 or the A400M but something faster, more violent, more precise. The noise arrives a half-second after the aircraft, a characteristic shriek of twin engines at military power at low altitude.]

[The first aircraft releases. Two AASM Hammer munitions drop, their propulsion kits igniting almost immediately, guiding them on their terminal approach to the target with GPS and infrared precision. The Rafale pulls up sharply, climbing away to the left.]

[A fraction of a second later — impact. The target position disappears inside two near-simultaneous explosions. Not a massive fireball — these are precision munitions, tightly placed. The building does not collapse dramatically. Its upper floors blow outward and inward. The reinforced position on the ground floor ceases to exist. Dust and smoke billow outward and upward in a dense column.]

[The second Rafale completes a follow-on pass, releasing a single additional round on a secondary position at the building's flank. Another precise impact. Another column of smoke.]

[Both aircraft pull up hard into the sky, their delta-wing planforms clean against the grey European overcast, engines still pushing hard. Within seconds they are climbing away, already a mile out, their shapes shrinking against the clouds.]

KERAUNOS LEAD:
(radio, unhurried)
AEGIS ACTUAL, KERAUNOS LEAD. Splash two. Target destroyed. BDA to follow. KERAUNOS FLIGHT is RTB. Bonne chance.

DUCKY:
(beat — watching the smoke column rise above the buildings ahead)
...Yeah. Thanks, Pierre.

[He stands, checks his weapon, looks at the squad.]

DUCKY:
(quiet, to the squad)
Alright. Let's go see what's left.

[AEGIS moves forward through the settling dust toward the destroyed position.]

VISUAL AND TONAL NOTES

The Rafale's character is defined by SPEED and PRECISION rather than scale. Fast, surgical, gone before the player fully processes it. Under 20 seconds from first visual contact to departure. The AASM Hammer impacts are precise and contained — devastating to the specific target, not spreading destruction across the surrounding street. A scalpel, not a hammer. The Rafale at low altitude produces a distinctive high-pitched twin-engine shriek very different from the turboprop rumble of the A400M or AC-130. Sound arrives slightly after the aircraft. Ducky's "Yeah. Thanks, Pierre." — deliberately casual. This is Ducky. The French pilot's "Bonne chance." — natural and unforced, a French pilot signing off in his own language.

CONTINUITY NOTE: This scene and Scene 6 (Zubr Landing) are causally linked — ARES tasks KERAUNOS at the end of the Zubr sequence. Seeding KERAUNOS assets in earlier missions recommended before this moment lands.


========================================================


SCENE 6 — THE ZUBR LANDING [FULL TREATMENT]
Vehicle: Zubr-class LCAC (x2 confirmed inbound, x1 third behind, Ropucha standing off)
Campaign: Do Right, Fear None (Ducky) — Game 1
Location: Dutch coastline near the Maasvlakte terminal, Rotterdam
Context: Pre-final mission escalation sequence

--------

CONTEXT AND NARRATIVE SETUP

AEGIS Squad is moving toward the Maasvlakte terminal — approaching through a coastal industrial area, exiting a treeline at the edge of dune terrain, or cresting an elevated road embankment that gives a sudden unobstructed view of the North Sea coastline. This is not a combat encounter. AEGIS watches and withdraws. The Russian amphibious force is too large to engage directly. The player sees what is coming and understands with complete clarity what the final mission is about to be.

THE SEQUENCE — FULL SCENE

[The squad moves along the edge of a coastal road or dune ridge. Industrial structures of the port complex are visible to the right. To the left, the North Sea. Grey sky, grey water, a cold Dutch coastal morning. Wind off the water. Flat, open, nowhere to hide.]

[Frost stops. He raises his rifle — not to shoot, but to look through the scope. He says nothing for a moment.]

FROST:
(quiet, almost to himself)
...Contact. Bearing two-seven-zero. Multiple surface contacts. Large.

[Ducky raises his own optics. What he sees through the scope — and what the camera then cuts to in a wide establishing shot — stops him cold.]

[Two Zubr-class LCACs are coming in from the northwest, riding low and fast over the grey water toward the Dutch beach below the terminal approach. They are enormous — 57 metres long, riding on a cushion of air and spray, their five gas turbine engines producing a sound unlike anything the squad has heard before: a deep, resonant, mechanical howl, felt in the chest before it's fully registered by the ears. The air cushion skirts billow white beneath them. The twin 30mm gun turrets forward are clearly visible, traversing slowly. The cargo ramps are still closed.]

[Behind the two lead Zubrs, further out to sea, more shapes are visible in the grey — a third Zubr, and beyond it the silhouette of a Ropucha-class landing ship standing off approximately two kilometres out.]

LUPIN:
(flat)
How many?

DUCKY:
(still looking through optics)
Two confirmed inbound. Third behind them. There's a Ropucha standing off — maybe two klicks out.

SWITCHBLADE:
(low)
What are they carrying?

DUCKY:
(beat)
Whatever they brought, it fits three tanks. Each.

[Silence. The squad watches. The Zubrs are closing fast — at 35 knots they cover the remaining distance in under two minutes. As they hit the shallow water approach to the beach the air cushion allows them to transition seamlessly from water to shore without slowing — they do not beach themselves the way conventional landing craft do. They simply continue forward, riding the cushion over the sand and gravel of the Dutch shoreline, the massive ramps dropping forward with a sound like a controlled explosion.]

[From the first Zubr's ramp: a T-80 main battle tank rolls forward onto Dutch soil, engine already running, followed immediately by a second. Infantry pour out from the sides — Russian Naval Infantry in full combat kit, spreading left and right into a perimeter, weapons up.]

[From the second Zubr: BTR-82 armoured vehicles rolling down the ramp in sequence, troops dismounting immediately and forming up.]

[The Grad rocket launchers — retracted during transit — are already beginning to elevate on one of the Zubrs, preparing to provide fire support for the landing force.]

[Ducky lowers his optics. He looks at the squad. Nobody speaks for a moment.]

DUCKY:
(to radio, steady)
ARES, this is AEGIS ACTUAL. We have eyes on a Russian amphibious landing — Zubr-class, at least two confirmed, third inbound. Armour and Naval Infantry on the beach. Grid to follow. How copy?

WALKER (ARES):
(radio, controlled)
AEGIS ACTUAL, ARES. Copy all. Hold your position. Do not engage. KERAUNOS is being tasked. Get me that grid.

DUCKY:
(already moving)
Frost. Grid.

FROST:
(already reading it off)
Copy.

[The squad pulls back from the ridge line, moving fast and low. Behind them, the sound of the Zubr turbines continues — that deep mechanical howl carrying across the flat Dutch coastal terrain, audible long after the craft themselves are out of sight. The Grad launchers fire — a rippling series of rockets arcing inland toward the terminal perimeter.]

[The final mission has begun whether AEGIS is ready or not.]

VISUAL AND TONAL NOTES

The Zubr's defining characteristic is its sheer improbability — something that large should not move that fast or transition from water to land that seamlessly. The scene is a pressure indicator, not a combat sequence — AEGIS watches and withdraws. The Ropucha standing off implies more coming. This is not the full picture. The Grad rockets firing at the terminal at the end is the transition moment — the final mission has started on the enemy's terms. Frost's first line — "...Contact. Bearing two-seven-zero. Multiple surface contacts. Large." — is the scene's ignition point. The word "Large" doing the work of an entire paragraph. This scene and Scene 5 (KERAUNOS) are causally linked — ARES tasks KERAUNOS at the end of this sequence.


========================================================


SCENE 7 — THE AC-130 SPECTRE CAS STRIKE [FULL TREATMENT]
Aircraft: AC-130 Spectre Gunship — SPECTRE FOUR ONE
Campaign: American Freedom (Romeo) — Game 2
Placement: TBD — tentatively late campaign, vehicle exfiltration under pursuit, possibly Frank rescue aftermath from Harlan

--------

CONCEPT

The scene lands with maximum impact because the player has earned it through sustained combat pressure. It is not spectacle inserted into a mission — it is the payoff for the player's effort. The AC-130 arrives because Romeo built something worth arriving for. The central image: Romeo on a mounted weapon in a vehicle moving downhill on a Kentucky county road, the hill's crest creating a natural horizon ahead. The AC-130 rises above that horizon line, flying toward the camera. Just before it reaches maximum visual presence it deploys flares — the iconic angel wing countermeasure smoke trail — flies through its own smoke, and continues.

PLAYER POSITION

Romeo is on a mounted weapon — M2 or similar — in the back of a pickup truck or similar vehicle moving fast downhill. The player has active control of the weapon throughout. The vehicle is moving; the player is managing the pursuit. The mounted weapon position gives the player the elevated sightline needed to see the horizon reveal when it happens.

TACTICAL CONTEXT

The AFC element is in a hot exfiltration — pursuit vehicles behind them, a county road descending a hill with open sky visible ahead. The situation is controlled but uncomfortable. A CAS request went up through Romeo's command two hours earlier. Whether it got processed and approved — whether an aircraft was actually tasked and launched — is genuinely uncertain. This uncertainty is the scene's dramatic engine.

DINGO:
(from the front of the vehicle)
"Command says SPECTRE is en route. Command also said that forty minutes ago."

RADIO SEQUENCE

SPECTRE FOUR ONE makes contact:

"ROMEO element, SPECTRE FOUR ONE, we are at your push frequency. Authenticate."

"ROMEO element authenticates KILO TANGO SEVEN. We have you loud and clear. Be advised we are mobile, south on county route twelve, taking fire from two to three pursuit vehicles, over."

"ROMEO element, copy. SPECTRE FOUR ONE is at angels two, four minutes out. We have your position on ROVER. Stand by, over."

Four minutes. The vehicle accelerates. The pursuit closes slightly on the descent. Romeo fires suppression bursts — not to destroy, to slow. To buy the four minutes.

On radio — F-16 tactical net bleeding briefly into Romeo's receiver, cross-channel bleed from congested airspace during active engagement:

"VIPER flight, BANDIT ONE is turning. He's coming back around—"
"VIPER TWO, I have him, stay with BANDIT TWO—"
"Fox two—"
"[Static]"

Then SPECTRE FOUR ONE again, calm, the specific calm of an AC-130 crew that has been doing this for a very long time:

"ROMEO element, SPECTRE FOUR ONE. One minute. We are in your twelve o'clock. You should have us shortly."

THE REVEAL — THE HORIZON

The player, on the mounted weapon, naturally looks forward — toward the horizon ahead, toward the clean line of the hill's descent against the open sky. Nothing yet. The pursuit vehicles still behind. Still closing. Thirty seconds.

Then — from the direction of the horizon ahead — a sound. Low. Pervasive. Not the sharp crack of jet engines but something broader, something with physical weight — four turboprop engines at combat power. Less a sound than a condition of the air. The player feels it before they see it.

The horizon line ahead — the clean edge of the hill's descent against the sky — begins to change. Something is rising above it. Something enormous.

THE AC-130 CRESTS THE HORIZON

Not fast — nothing about an AC-130 in flight reads as fast, because the aircraft is so large that its speed becomes relative to its size rather than to anything human-scaled. It rises above the hill's horizon the way a ship rises above the curvature of the ocean — slowly, massively, inevitable.

It is flying toward the vehicle. Toward the player. Growing in the frame as it descends toward them on its attack approach. The four propeller discs catching the light. The fuselage enormous and grey and bristling with sensor pods and weapons systems. The 105mm howitzer on the port side fires. The player doesn't see the round. They see the result: the lead pursuit vehicle disappearing in a column of fire and debris fifty metres behind the player's truck.

Then the second vehicle. Gone.

The AC-130 passes directly overhead. For a moment the aircraft fills the frame — a ceiling of grey fuselage and propeller noise and the smell of exhaust. Then past, banking slowly to the left, beginning its circuit.

THE FLARES — THE ANGEL WING

A Su-30 that has been tracking the tactical area for the past ninety seconds locks the AC-130. The aircraft's threat detection system responds immediately. The flares deploy — not one or two but a full defensive salvo, arcing outward from both wingtips simultaneously in the specific spread pattern that gives the countermeasure its silhouette.

CAMERA NOTE — THE FOUR SECONDS

The moment the flares deploy, the camera stops tracking the vehicle entirely and simply looks up. Not dramatically, not with a sudden cut — it drifts upward the way a person's attention drifts upward when something overhead demands it, then holds. The vehicle continues moving beneath the frame. The pursuit is irrelevant. The road is irrelevant.

For approximately four seconds, the only thing in the frame is the AC-130 and the flares and the smoke and the Kentucky sky. Four seconds is a long time in an action sequence. The player retains control of the mounted weapon during it — they could technically be doing something tactical. But they won't be. Nobody will be. Because what's overhead is more important than anything on the road.

That involuntary cessation of tactical thinking is the scene's real achievement. For four seconds, Romeo stops being a soldier and becomes a witness. The player stops playing and starts watching.

Then the smoke begins to diffuse. The aircraft banks away. The road comes back. The mission continues.

RESOLUTION

The Su-30 pulls up hard. The flares have done their work. The missile seeker confused and then lost. VIPER ONE back on him. The engagement moves north — away from the road, away from the vehicle, away from the AC-130 which is now banking slowly, enormously, to come back around for another attack pass if needed.

"ROMEO element, SPECTRE FOUR ONE. BANDITS are egressing. You are clear. What else do you need, over?"

A beat. Romeo looks at the road ahead.

"SPECTRE FOUR ONE, I think we're good. How copy?"

"ROMEO element, copy good. SPECTRE FOUR ONE will remain on station. You call, we answer. Over."

"Thank you, SPECTRE FOUR ONE."

A brief pause. Then, from the AC-130:

"Don't mention it. American Freedom, over."

THE 'AMERICAN FREEDOM' LINE

Not a triumphant callback. Not a winking acknowledgment. The specific thing that a crew says when they know who they're talking to and want them to know they know. The AC-130 crew has been following the AFC's story. Every American service member in the theater knows the name — because Crodyn put it on television.

The crew saying it back to Romeo — over a military radio net, on the record, using the designation that the President of the United States just called a terrorist organization — is a small act of institutional defiance that costs the crew nothing in the moment and means everything to the player who has lived inside this campaign.

It also means something for the wider story: Romeo's command will hear that exchange. Crodyn's intelligence apparatus, monitoring military communications, will hear it too. The AC-130 crew just put themselves on the wrong side of a presidential designation, knowingly, over an open tactical frequency. They knew what they were doing. That is the point.

CLOSING IMAGE

The vehicle continues down the road. Behind them, the smoke trail from the flares is still visible — the angel wing silhouette slowly diffusing in the morning air, the shape holding longer than seems physically reasonable, as if the sky is reluctant to let it go. Romeo watches it from the mounted weapon. The radio continues its work. The mission continues its work. The smoke fades. The AC-130 banks and holds its orbit, patient, overhead.


========================================================
END OF DOCUMENT

SCENE STATUS SUMMARY:
