[DOC-020]
Original filename: ProjectWarriors_EpicScenes_AllSix.txt
Category: Scenes / mission content
File type: TXT
Size: 20205 bytes
SHA-256 prefix: 85e0ab2401d4b84a
First non-empty line: PROJECT WARRIORS — EPIC VEHICLE & AIRCRAFT SCENE DESCRIPTIONS
Duplicate status: Unique content entry

BEGIN SOURCE CONTENT
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PROJECT WARRIORS — EPIC VEHICLE & AIRCRAFT SCENE DESCRIPTIONS
Compiled from Meta Thread Development
All six scenes — master document
========================================================


SCENE 1 — THE AC-130 FLYOVER CHASE (Romeo's Campaign, Game 2 — American Freedom)
Aircraft: AC-130 Gunship
Location: Harlan County, Kentucky (near Calloway and Redbud)
Mission context: Following the rescue of Aldrich / late campaign sequence

Description:
After freeing Aldrich, Romeo's team is in a vehicle being pursued by Russian forces through the Kentucky countryside. The pursuit vehicles are UAZ-type light trucks with mounted guns — fast enough to maintain pressure, not fast enough to fully close the gap on Romeo's vehicle running at full speed. Multiple vehicles in pursuit, at least one with an active mounted gun continuing to engage the player throughout the chase.

At a dramatic moment during the chase, a US Air Force AC-130 gunship (callsign to be determined) makes a low, slow pass overhead — appearing suddenly over the ridgeline or treeline. The aircraft is massive, close, and loud. It descends to a dangerously low altitude directly over or adjacent to the road, its engines shaking the air. The image of a slow, enormous turboprop military gunship appearing at low altitude over a typical Kentucky rural landscape — fields, farmhouses, winding roads — is deliberately jarring and cinematic.

The AC-130 proceeds to engage the pursuing Russian vehicles, eliminating or scattering them and breaking off the chase.

Narrative mechanic / how the pilots got there:
Earlier missions in Romeo's American Freedom campaign (likely Dead Air or a related mission) inadvertently created a communications benefit for US Armed Forces operating in the region — Romeo's resistance cell actions disrupted or intercepted enemy communications in a way that gave US forces an unexpected operational advantage, possibly enabling the capture or denial of a strategically important position. This created an informal awareness among US military elements of who Romeo's group is and what they are doing.

This flyover occurs BEFORE President Crodyn's wartime address declaring the AFC a domestic terrorist organization. The pilots are therefore still operating in a grey zone where supporting what appears to be American resistance fighters feels permissible — they have a hunch about who these people are, they've heard enough through operational channels to make an educated guess, and they act on it. After the Crodyn declaration, the same pilots could no longer make the same call.

The pilots spot Romeo's team being pursued, radio it in, receive permission to divert and provide close air support, and route to their location.

Visual and tonal notes:
- The image of the AC-130 at low altitude over rural Kentucky is intended as a striking, almost surreal visual — familiar American landscape suddenly occupied by an instrument of war
- Flagged as strong trailer / promotional asset material
- The slow, deliberate approach of the aircraft contrasts with the speed and chaos of the chase sequence below it
- Sound design critical — the deep rumble of four turboprop engines at low altitude should be physically felt by the player before the aircraft is fully visible


========================================================


SCENE 2 — THE A400M FLYOVER (General world-building / promotional concept)
Aircraft: Airbus A400M Atlas (DAOG designation: ICARUS)

Description:
A massive turboprop military transport aircraft — the Airbus A400M — makes a slow, low pass directly overhead of the player's position in a recognizably ordinary American suburban environment. The contrast between the familiar domestic landscape below and the scale and weight of the military aircraft overhead is the entire point of the image.

The A400M is enormous and slow relative to jet aircraft. At low altitude its four large turboprop engines produce a distinctive, deep, resonant sound unlike anything most civilians would have heard at close range. The aircraft fills the frame. It is close enough that markings and details are visible.

This image — a giant NATO military transport at low altitude over American suburbia — is one of the defining visual expressions of the game's core theme: the collision of the familiar and the catastrophic. The world has not waited. The war has come here.

Flagged as a key promotional and trailer asset. Encapsulates the scale of the conflict and the surreal quality of invasion on American soil in a single wordless shot.

DAOG asset designation: ICARUS (Airbus A400M) — part of the HERMES airlift component of DAOG Command's force structure.


========================================================


SCENE 3 — THE AC-130 ATTACK RUN (General world-building / promotional concept)
Aircraft: AC-130 Gunship

Description:
An AC-130 gunship passes at low altitude on an attack run over or near a typical American suburban neighborhood. The image of the aircraft — its guns active or implied — against the backdrop of ordinary American houses, yards, and streets is deliberately dissonant.

Paired conceptually with the A400M image as part of the broader visual language of the game: large, slow, purposeful military aircraft operating at low altitude over recognizably American civilian environments. The scale of the machines against the domestic scale of the landscape is the emotional payload.

Both the A400M and AC-130 images invoke the Tears in the Rain / Roy Batty thematic underpinning of the studio identity. The player gets to witness things that feel impossible and yet are happening.


========================================================


SCENE 4 — RED DAWN CALLBACK — ENEMY PARATROOPER DROP (Romeo's Campaign, Game 2 — American Freedom)
Location: Smoky Mountains, visible from distance during navigation moment

Description:
At a specific point during Romeo's American Freedom campaign in Game 2, the player — while navigating on foot through terrain — spots in the distance over the Smoky Mountains a formation of enemy paratroopers descending. The parachutes are visible at distance, a deliberate callback to the 1984 film Red Dawn.

This image serves a dual narrative purpose:
1. In-world navigation device — the player sees where the paratroopers are landing and understands instinctively that this is where the mission is heading
2. Deliberate visual homage to Red Dawn — designed to be felt rather than stated. No dialogue draws attention to it

Flagged as strong trailer and promotional asset material — specifically as a standalone rendered version for use in teasers. Suggested trailer treatment: shot opens on the Smoky Mountains peaceful and still, then paratroopers begin to appear — first one, then dozens. Music shift completes the moment.

Works for players who know Red Dawn and works independently as a striking image for those who don't. The reference should never be made explicit in dialogue or any other in-game element.


========================================================


SCENE 5 — KERAUNOS URBAN PRECISION STRIKE (Ducky's Campaign, Game 2 — Persistent Threat)
Aircraft: Dassault Rafale B (x2)
DAOG Designation: KERAUNOS
Nationality: French Air and Space Force
Role: Close Air Support / Precision Ground Attack
Weapons: AASM Hammer precision air-to-ground munitions
Location: Urban / built-up environment in Western Europe (specific city TBD)

Context and narrative setup:
Ducky and AEGIS Squad are pinned down by a fortified Russian or enemy position in a dense urban environment — a reinforced building, a blocked street corridor, a bridge approach, or a key infrastructure chokepoint. Too heavily defended for AEGIS to take by direct assault. Ducky or Lt. Tara Halliday (ORACLE) calls in the strike through DAOG Command channels. Colonel Mark Walker (ARES) approves. KERAUNOS FLIGHT acknowledges and begins their attack run. The player, as Ducky, is ordered to pull back to a safe observation distance and hold.

---

THE STRIKE SEQUENCE — FULL SCENE:

[The squad takes cover behind a low wall or in a doorway with a clear line of sight to the target building approximately 200-300 metres ahead. The street between them and the target is empty — rubble, abandoned vehicles, broken glass. It is quiet for a moment, the kind of quiet that precedes something.]

DUCKY:
(into radio, clipped and dry)
KERAUNOS FLIGHT, this is AEGIS ACTUAL. Target is marked. You are clear hot. How copy?

KERAUNOS LEAD:
(French-accented English, calm and professional, slight static on the radio)
AEGIS ACTUAL, KERAUNOS LEAD. Copy clear hot. Tally the mark. Running in now. Stand by.

[A beat. Silence. Then — heard before seen — a rising, tearing sound from the west. High and fast. Both Rafales come in low and fast over the rooftops, in close formation, wings loaded with AASM Hammer munitions, the Thales Damoclès targeting pods visible under the fuselage. They are moving at speed — not the slow, gravitational presence of the AC-130 or the A400M but something faster, more violent, more precise. The noise arrives a half-second after the aircraft, a characteristic shriek of twin engines at military power at low altitude.]

[The first aircraft releases. Two AASM Hammer munitions drop, their propulsion kits igniting almost immediately, guiding them on their terminal approach to the target with GPS and infrared precision. The Rafale pulls up sharply, climbing away to the left.]

[A fraction of a second later — impact. The target position disappears inside two near-simultaneous explosions. Not a massive fireball — these are precision munitions, tightly placed. The building does not collapse dramatically. Its upper floors blow outward and inward. The reinforced position on the ground floor ceases to exist. Dust and smoke billow outward and upward in a dense column.]

[The second Rafale completes a follow-on pass, releasing a single additional round on a secondary position at the building's flank. Another precise impact. Another column of smoke.]

[Both aircraft pull up hard into the sky, their delta-wing planforms clean against the grey European overcast, engines still pushing hard. Within seconds they are climbing away, already a mile out, their shapes shrinking against the clouds.]

KERAUNOS LEAD:
(radio, unhurried)
AEGIS ACTUAL, KERAUNOS LEAD. Splash two. Target destroyed. BDA to follow. KERAUNOS FLIGHT is RTB. Bonne chance.

DUCKY:
(beat — watching the smoke column rise above the buildings ahead)
...Yeah. Thanks, Pierre.

[He stands, checks his weapon, looks at the squad.]

DUCKY:
(quiet, to the squad)
Alright. Let's go see what's left.

[AEGIS moves forward through the settling dust toward the destroyed position.]

---

Visual and tonal notes:
- The Rafale's character in this scene is defined by SPEED and PRECISION rather than scale. Fast, surgical, and gone before the player has fully processed what happened. The strike is over in under 20 seconds from first visual contact.
- The Rafale's distinctive delta-canard planform is immediately recognizable and unmistakably French. French Air and Space Force roundels and grey/blue-grey livery visible in the brief seconds overhead.
- AASM Hammer impacts: precise, contained, devastating to the specific target. Not spreading destruction across the surrounding street. This is a scalpel, not a hammer.
- Sound design critical. The Rafale at low altitude produces a distinctive high-pitched twin-engine shriek very different from the deep turboprop rumble of the A400M or AC-130. Sound arrives slightly after the aircraft.
- Ducky's "Yeah. Thanks, Pierre." — deliberately casual and characteristically understated. This is Ducky.
- The French pilot's "Bonne chance." — natural and unforced. A French pilot signing off in his own language. Clean and real.
- The column of smoke rising above the European urban skyline is the lasting image of this scene.

Location note: Specific city TBD pending further development of Ducky's Persistent Threat campaign geography. Candidate environments: a Dutch port city, a Baltic coastal city, or a Central European urban centre. Scene is written to be location-agnostic.

Continuity note: KERAUNOS (Dassault Rafale B) confirmed in the DAOG Command force structure under Close Air Support alongside PHAETON (JAS 39 Gripen). Seeding in earlier missions recommended — a radio reference, a mention from ORACLE that KERAUNOS assets are available — before this moment lands.


========================================================


SCENE 6 — THE ZUBR LANDING (Ducky's Campaign, Game 1 — Do Right, Fear None)
Vehicle: Zubr-class LCAC (x2 confirmed inbound, x1 third behind, Ropucha standing off)
Location: Dutch coastline near the Maasvlakte terminal, Rotterdam
Mission context: Pre-final mission escalation sequence — pressure indicator before the terminal defense mission

Context and narrative setup:
AEGIS Squad is moving toward the Maasvlakte terminal — approaching through a coastal industrial area, exiting a treeline at the edge of dune terrain, or cresting an elevated road embankment that gives a sudden unobstructed view of the North Sea coastline and the shallow beach approaches to the terminal.

This is not a combat encounter. AEGIS watches and withdraws. The Russian amphibious force is too large to engage directly. The player sees what is coming and understands with complete clarity what the final mission is about to be.

---

THE SEQUENCE — FULL SCENE:

[The squad moves along the edge of a coastal road or dune ridge. Industrial structures of the port complex are visible to the right. To the left, the North Sea. Grey sky, grey water, a cold Dutch coastal morning. Wind off the water. Flat, open, nowhere to hide.]

[Frost stops. He raises his rifle — not to shoot, but to look through the scope. He says nothing for a moment.]

FROST:
(quiet, almost to himself)
...Contact. Bearing two-seven-zero. Multiple surface contacts. Large.

[Ducky raises his own optics. What he sees through the scope — and what the camera then cuts to in a wide establishing shot — stops him cold.]

[Two Zubr-class LCACs are coming in from the northwest, riding low and fast over the grey water toward the Dutch beach below the terminal approach. They are enormous — 57 metres long, riding on a cushion of air and spray, their five gas turbine engines producing a sound unlike anything the squad has heard before: a deep, resonant, mechanical howl, felt in the chest before it's fully registered by the ears. The air cushion skirts billow white beneath them. The twin 30mm gun turrets forward are clearly visible, traversing slowly. The cargo ramps are still closed.]

[Behind the two lead Zubrs, further out to sea, more shapes are visible in the grey — a third Zubr, and beyond it the silhouette of a Ropucha-class landing ship standing off approximately two kilometres out.]

LUPIN:
(flat)
How many?

DUCKY:
(still looking through optics)
Two confirmed inbound. Third behind them. There's a Ropucha standing off — maybe two klicks out.

SWITCHBLADE:
(low)
What are they carrying?

DUCKY:
(beat)
Whatever they brought, it fits three tanks. Each.

[Silence. The squad watches. The Zubrs are closing fast — at 35 knots they cover the remaining distance in under two minutes. As they hit the shallow water approach to the beach the air cushion allows them to transition seamlessly from water to shore without slowing — they do not beach themselves the way conventional landing craft do. They simply continue forward, riding the cushion over the sand and gravel of the Dutch shoreline, the massive ramps dropping forward with a sound like a controlled explosion.]

[From the first Zubr's ramp: a T-80 main battle tank rolls forward onto Dutch soil, engine already running, followed immediately by a second. Infantry pour out from the sides — Russian Naval Infantry in full combat kit, spreading left and right into a perimeter, weapons up.]

[From the second Zubr: BTR-82 armoured vehicles rolling down the ramp in sequence, troops dismounting immediately and forming up.]

[The Grad rocket launchers — retracted during transit — are already beginning to elevate on one of the Zubrs, preparing to provide fire support for the landing force.]

[Ducky lowers his optics. He looks at the squad. Nobody speaks for a moment.]

DUCKY:
(to radio, steady)
ARES, this is AEGIS ACTUAL. We have eyes on a Russian amphibious landing — Zubr-class, at least two confirmed, third inbound. Armour and Naval Infantry on the beach. Grid to follow. How copy?

WALKER (ARES):
(radio, controlled)
AEGIS ACTUAL, ARES. Copy all. Hold your position. Do not engage. KERAUNOS is being tasked. Get me that grid.

DUCKY:
(already moving)
Frost. Grid.

FROST:
(already reading it off)
Copy.

[The squad pulls back from the ridge line, moving fast and low. Behind them, the sound of the Zubr turbines continues — that deep mechanical howl carrying across the flat Dutch coastal terrain, audible long after the craft themselves are out of sight. The Grad launchers fire — a rippling series of rockets arcing inland toward the terminal perimeter.]

[The final mission has begun whether AEGIS is ready or not.]

---

Visual and tonal notes:
- The Zubr's defining visual characteristic is its sheer improbability — something that large should not move that fast or transition from water to land that seamlessly. The air cushion skirt billowing white underneath it, the spray trail behind it, the turbine howl — these details make the image unforgettable. Most players will never have seen a Zubr before. This is their introduction to it and it should feel like a revelation.
- The scene is a pressure indicator, not a combat sequence. AEGIS watches and withdraws. The enemy force is too large to engage here — that's the point. The player sees what they're about to fight and feels the weight of it before the mission begins.
- The Ropucha-class landing ship standing off in the background implies more forces in reserve. The Zubrs are the fast forward element. There is more coming. This is not the full picture.
- The Grad rockets firing at the terminal at the end of the sequence is the transition moment — the final mission has started on the enemy's terms. No pause, no preparation time.
- Sound design critical. The Zubr uses five gas turbines — three for propulsion and two for the air cushion lift system, each delivering approximately 12,100 shaft horsepower. The sound at close range on a flat coastal environment would be extraordinary — felt physically as much as heard. Present in the scene from the moment Frost first spots them, growing as they close the distance.
- The Ropucha standing off in the background implies there is more coming behind the Zubrs. The player does not see everything. That incompleteness is part of the dread.
- Frost's first line — "Contact. Bearing two-seven-zero. Multiple surface contacts. Large." — is the scene's emotional ignition point. The word "large" doing the work of an entire paragraph.
- The Dutch coastal terrain — flat, open, industrial, dunes and beach and port infrastructure — gives the scene a specific recognizable geography. The flatness means the Zubrs are visible from a long distance, giving the player time to process what they're seeing before the scale of it fully registers.
- This scene also serves as a continuity bridge to Scene 5 (KERAUNOS) — ARES tasks KERAUNOS assets at the end of this sequence, implying the Rafales are being sent to deal with the landing force. The two scenes are causally linked.

Continuity note:
The Ropucha-class landing ship standing off is a real Russian Navy vessel class used for amphibious operations and is consistent with the Baltic Fleet operational context established in Ducky's Game 1 campaign. The combination of Zubr LCACs for fast shallow-water landing and a Ropucha for heavier equipment delivery is historically accurate Russian amphibious doctrine.


========================================================
END OF DOCUMENT — 6 SCENES TOTAL
========================================================
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
END SOURCE CONTENT

ANGEL — CINEMATIC SCREENPLAY PASS
Project Warriors — Game 2 — Romeo Campaign
Late Act 2 / Exfil Chase Set Piece

CANON LOCK
- Location thread: post-liberation AFC operation tied to Aldridge
- Vehicle: current-generation Ford F-150, quad cab
- Mount: improvised bed-mounted ring / pintle
- Weapon: M240B
- Ammo state: two cans total
- Player position: Romeo on mounted gun
- Pursuit: three enemy UAZ-type vehicles, at least one with mounted gun
- Air support: AC-130 Spectre gunship, callsign SPECTRE FOUR ONE

NOTE
This pass is written as an in-engine cinematic/gameplay hybrid rather than a non-interactive cutscene. The player should remain in control for most of the sequence, especially the reveal.

======================================================================
EXT. KENTUCKY COUNTY ROAD - DAY
======================================================================

A battered FORD F-150 tears downhill along a narrow Kentucky road bordered by pasture fence, brush, and tree line. Dust boils behind it. The truck is civilian at its core, but changed by necessity: improvised mount in the bed, welds visible, metal scraped raw at the joints, gear lashed down wherever it will fit.

ROMEO is on the mounted M240B in the truck bed, braced inside the ring mount, one boot slipping half an inch every time the rear axle kicks sideways over a rut.

The truck is already under fire.

Rounds crack past the cab. A rear window spiders. Fence posts flick past in a strobing rhythm.

                               DRIVER
                 Contact rear! Rear, rear, rear!

                               FRONT PASSENGER
                 They stayed on us!

                               AMMO TEAMMATE
                 Romeo, on the gun!

Romeo hauls the weapon around toward the rear arc.

Down the road behind them: a DUST PLUME, then the first UAZ breaks through it, hard and fast. A second appears on the bend behind it. Then a third, offset wide, rising and falling with the road.

                               FRONT PASSENGER
                 One truck--

                               ALDRIDGE
                 No. Three. Three total.

A burst from the lead vehicle walks up the road and snaps over the truck bed.

                               DRIVER
                 Lead one's mounted!

Romeo settles the sights.

                               AMMO TEAMMATE
                 Romeo! Two cans total!

That lands harder than the incoming fire.

Romeo opens up in short, controlled bursts. The M240B pounds through the chassis. Brass rattles across the truck bed and vanishes into the road behind them.

The lead UAZ shudders under the impacts. The enemy gunner ducks. The windshield crazes.

                               DRIVER
                 Lead gun truck! Kill that gun!

                               ALDRIDGE
                 Don't chase all three. Break the one that can kill us.

The road bends. The truck leans hard. Romeo has to fight the mount and the road at the same time.

                               AMMO TEAMMATE
                 Short bursts!

The second UAZ starts offsetting for angle. The third hangs back just enough to be trouble later.

Romeo bursts again -- this time longer, less clean. The ring mount clatters. The truck drops into a washout and slams out of it. The weapon bucks off target.

                               DRIVER
                 Hold on!

                               ALDRIDGE
                 Road drops here!

The lead gun truck recovers and answers with another burst. A round punches through thin sheet metal somewhere behind Romeo with an ugly, intimate sound.

Romeo keeps firing.

The belt runs dry.

A dead click.

For one sharp instant the whole chase becomes enormous.

                               ROMEO / AMMO TEAMMATE
                 Reloading!

                               DRIVER
                 Make it fast!

                               ALDRIDGE
                 They're gaining!

Romeo ducks into the ring. The feed cover comes up. The AMMO TEAMMATE wrestles the next can upward from the cab/bed handoff position, one hand braced, one hand fighting the vibration of the truck.

                               AMMO TEAMMATE
                 Hold it steady -- hold it steady--

                               DRIVER
                 I am!

The truck hits another bump. The belt slips. Romeo reseats it with a hard slap, slams the cover shut, charges the weapon, and comes back up on the gun just as the second UAZ closes the gap.

He fires again. The second belt starts to disappear.

The middle phase of the chase is worse than the beginning. The Russians are not just chasing. They are learning the truck's rhythm, its weak windows, its bad angles.

One UAZ holds center. One drifts wide. One pressures from behind the others, waiting for the reload that may or may not come.

Inside the cab, the FRONT PASSENGER fights the radio.

                               FRONT PASSENGER
                 Command says SPECTRE may be on call.

                               DRIVER
                 May?

                               FRONT PASSENGER
                 That's what I got.

Romeo kills the gunner in the lead truck or suppresses him hard enough to matter. Another burst punches into the second vehicle's front end and throws smoke off the hood. But the third remains. And the second is still moving.

The road straightens just enough to show the geometry of the problem.

Not enough gun.
Not enough time.
Not enough road.

                               ALDRIDGE
                 Only shoot what matters!

                               DRIVER
                 Pick one and break it!

Romeo does. He has to.

The belt count drops.

                               DRIVER
                 How much you got left?

                               AMMO TEAMMATE
                 Not enough!

Rounds tear through the tailgate. The truck fishtails half a lane and recovers.

The second belt is almost gone.

Romeo ducks again for the final handoff.

The AMMO TEAMMATE shoves the can up toward him, arm stretched, shoulder jammed against the frame.

                               AMMO TEAMMATE
                 That's the last can. Make it count.

No one answers. No one needs to.

Romeo seats the belt and comes back onto the gun.

Everything now is triage.

A burst into the most dangerous truck.
A burst to keep the offset vehicle from getting too comfortable.
A burst saved because there may not be another.

The windshield in front of the driver is cracked through the center now. One side mirror is gone. The ring mount shudders like it wants to tear free from the truck bed.

                               DRIVER
                 We are not doing this much longer!

                               ALDRIDGE
                 Stay on the road!

The FRONT PASSENGER freezes, head tilted to the headset.

                               FRONT PASSENGER
                 Wait. Wait one--

Then, over the radio -- calm, clipped, unmistakably professional:

                               SPECTRE FOUR ONE (RADIO)
                 ROMEO element, SPECTRE FOUR ONE, we are at your
                 push frequency. Authenticate.

The truck is still under fire.

The FRONT PASSENGER keys the handset.

                               FRONT PASSENGER
                 SPECTRE FOUR ONE, this is ROMEO element.
                 Authenticate Sierra-Two-Kilo.

A burst from behind forces Romeo to duck the weapon a fraction. He fires back without really seeing.

The reply comes quickly.

                               SPECTRE FOUR ONE (RADIO)
                 ROMEO element, copy. SPECTRE FOUR ONE is at angels
                 two, four minutes out. We have your position on
                 ROVER. Stand by, over.

The words help. They do not solve anything yet.

The truck barrels into the final downhill stretch. Trees thin. The road ahead opens.

The sound changes first.

Not the high whine of jets. Not the chopping violence of rotor blades. Something heavier. Slower. Turboprop mass. The kind of sound that seems to come through the air and the earth at the same time.

                               SPECTRE FOUR ONE (RADIO)
                 ROMEO element, SPECTRE FOUR ONE. One minute. We are
                 in your twelve o'clock. You should have us shortly.

A beat.

                               ALDRIDGE / DRIVER
                 You hear that?

Romeo does.

He swings his attention forward.

The road drops away in front of them toward an open horizon line framed by low hills, fence line, and morning sky.

For a fraction of a second there is nothing there.

Then the AC-130 begins to rise over the ridgeline.

Not fast. Nothing that large looks fast. It lifts over the horizon like a ship rising over the curve of the sea -- slow, heavy, inevitable.

For a moment the whole chase reorders itself around that single fact.

The aircraft grows.

Grey fuselage. Prop arcs. Immense wingspan. Not a rescue helicopter darting low, not a fast mover slashing through and vanishing, but a giant American gunship coming straight into the frame over rural Kentucky.

Just before it reaches maximum visual presence --

FLARES.

A full defensive salvo bursts from both sides in a wide, symmetrical spread.

Smoke trails bloom into the angel-wing silhouette.

For several seconds the only thing that matters is the aircraft and the flares and the smoke and the Kentucky sky.

Romeo still has the gun in his hands. He could technically be shooting.

He doesn't.

Nobody would.

The AC-130 roars overhead.

Then the strikes begin.

Behind the truck, one UAZ disappears in a blast of dust, fire, and broken metal. Another slews sideways, disabled, and tumbles off the edge of the road. The last breaks formation, swerving hard, suddenly unsure whether survival still exists in the same shape it did ten seconds earlier.

On the radio:

                               SPECTRE FOUR ONE (RADIO)
                 ROMEO element, SPECTRE FOUR ONE. BANDITS are
                 egressing. You are clear. What else do you need, over?

The truck keeps moving. The team is still breathing hard, still in it, but alive now in a different way.

                               FRONT PASSENGER / ROMEO
                 SPECTRE FOUR ONE, I think we're good. How copy?

                               SPECTRE FOUR ONE (RADIO)
                 ROMEO element, copy good. SPECTRE FOUR ONE will
                 remain on station. You call, we answer. Over.

A beat.

                               FRONT PASSENGER / ROMEO
                 Thank you, SPECTRE FOUR ONE.

Another brief pause. Then:

                               SPECTRE FOUR ONE (RADIO)
                 Don't mention it. American Freedom, over.

No one in the truck says anything for a second.

The AC-130 banks into orbit above and behind them, enormous and patient.

The angel-wing smoke still hangs in the air longer than it should.

The truck rattles on.

                               DRIVER
                 Everybody still here?

                               ALDRIDGE
                 Yeah.

A beat. Aldridge looks up once, almost despite himself.

                               ALDRIDGE
                 Hell of a thing.

The truck turns off the main road onto a narrower concealed route, disappearing under tree cover.

The gunship remains overhead.

FADE OUT.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
END SOURCE CONTENT

HUDSON OVERLOOK
Clean Screenplay-Style Narrative Document

Date: Labor Day — September 3, 2029
Perspective: First-person, anonymous civilian
Format: Interactive narrative cold open
Length target: 6–8 minutes
Tone arc: ordinary life -> subtle wrongness -> distant dread -> sudden fear -> systemic realization -> hard cut

CAST

PLAYER CHARACTER
Anonymous male civilian, first-person POV.

TANYA
Player’s girlfriend. Warm, playful, then frightened.

LOUIS
Perceptive, practical, first to sense danger.

JANINE
Phone-focused, casual, socially expressive.

VERONICA
Quieter, observant, composed until panic breaks through.

OPENING PRINCIPLE

The player should not feel like a soldier or protagonist yet.
He should feel like he is already in the middle of a real day off.

No tactical framing.
No score until the run back to the car.
No overt exposition.

SCENE 1 — TRAILHEAD PICNIC AREA

EXT. HUDSON OVERLOOK TRAILHEAD — AFTERNOON

Late summer light. Mild breeze. Leaves moving overhead. Insects. A faint hush of distant traffic somewhere beyond the woods.

FADE IN:

FIRST-PERSON POV.

The player sits at a weathered public picnic table with attached benches. On the tabletop: a folded trail map, half-finished drinks, sunglasses, an empty snack wrapper.

TANYA sits across from the player. JANINE and VERONICA sit along one side of the table. LOUIS stands nearby, adjusting a light backpack, waiting for the group to get moving.

For the first few seconds, the player has LOOK CONTROL ONLY.

Tanya reaches for the empty snack wrapper, lifts it, and looks at the player.

TANYA
I can’t believe you ate the last Twistie.

PLAYER
I was hungry.

TANYA
That’s not a defense.

JANINE
I’m with her, honestly.

VERONICA
You always take the last one and then act surprised when people notice.

PLAYER
That feels made up.

TANYA
Wow.

Louis checks his watch or phone and looks over.

LOUIS
Come on, guys. We’re gonna miss the movie.

JANINE
No, no, I can still get tickets.

She taps her phone.

JANINE
Probably.

LOUIS
That is not confidence.

TANYA
We drove all this way and we’re still gonna sprint from a scenic overlook to a mediocre theater because Janine buys tickets like it’s an emergency landing.

JANINE
It’s called spontaneity.

VERONICA
It’s called bad planning.

Light laughter.

A subtle gameplay prompt appears:

[STAND UP]

The player presses input.

The camera rises naturally from the bench.

SCENE 2 — THE TRAIL

EXT. WOODED TRAIL — CONTINUOUS

The group begins moving down the trail at an easy pace. Warm green light. Packed dirt underfoot. Occasional breaks in the trees hint at a steep drop and water in the distance.

The player now has FULL WALK AND LOOK CONTROL.
SPRINT IS DISABLED.

A minimal objective appears:

FOLLOW YOUR FRIENDS

The group naturally spaces itself:
Louis slightly ahead.
Tanya near the player.
Janine intermittently checking her phone.
Veronica alternating between the middle and rear.

Ambient walking dialogue plays with pauses and overlap.

TANYA
You really ate all of them?

PLAYER
There were like three left.

TANYA
There were four.

PLAYER
That sounds unverifiable.

TANYA
I counted.

PLAYER
That’s insane.

TANYA
That’s survival.

They keep walking.

JANINE
If they’re sold out, I’m blaming all of you for making me go outside.

VERONICA
You suggested this.

JANINE
I suggest a lot of things. That doesn’t make me responsible for them.

LOUIS
That’s not how that works.

At a scenic opening, Tanya drifts to the player’s side and lifts her phone.

TANYA
Okay, wait. Stop for a second.

She frames a photo.

TANYA
Don’t do the face.

PLAYER
What face?

TANYA
That one.

She takes the picture.

TANYA
Yeah, that’s terrible. Perfect.

They continue.

Leaves. Wind. Footsteps. Birds. Still no score.

About halfway through the walk, Janine slows and frowns at her phone.

JANINE
Hey. Do you guys have signal?

LOUIS
Out here? Probably not.

JANINE
No, like— nothing. Not even one bar.

Veronica checks her own phone.

VERONICA
Mine too.

Tanya glances at hers and shrugs.

TANYA
We’re still in the woods.

JANINE
The city’s right there, though.

LOUIS
We’re on a hillside in the middle of trees. Try again at the overlook.

JANINE
I am trying again at the overlook. That’s literally my plan.

They keep walking.

Nobody treats it like a crisis yet.

If the player falls behind too long, one of the group calls back casually:

TANYA (O.S.)
You coming?

or

LOUIS (O.S.)
Come on, man.

SCENE 3 — APPROACH TO THE OVERLOOK

EXT. APPROACH TRAIL — CONTINUOUS

The trail widens subtly. More light ahead. The wind is a little stronger here.

Conversation thins out naturally.

Louis slows first.

LOUIS
...Huh.

TANYA
What?

Louis looks through the trees but does not answer.

The player rounds the final bend.

Ahead is a modest entry threshold to the overlook platform — a narrow opening between low stonework that funnels movement naturally.

The group moves toward it.

SCENE 4 — THE OVERLOOK REVEAL

EXT. HUDSON OVERLOOK PLATFORM — CONTINUOUS

The player steps out onto the overlook.

Below: a broad river.
Beyond: a distant city skyline.

At first glance the view is simply wide and beautiful enough to require a second look.

Then the wrongness resolves.

Several smoke columns rise from different parts of the city.
Not one central fire.
Scattered fires.
Isolated plumes.
Small, strange movements in the far air that are too distant to identify cleanly.

A few bystanders are already at the overlook barrier:
One holding up a phone.
Another squinting toward the city.
An older man stepping forward for a better angle.
A couple murmuring to one another.

The player has FULL LOOK CONTROL and LIMITED MOVEMENT.

No one immediately understands what they are seeing.

TANYA
What is that?

JANINE
Is that smoke?

VERONICA
From where?

BYSTANDER 1
Was there an explosion or something?

BYSTANDER 2
That’s... more than one.

Louis steps closer to the low barrier.

LOUIS
No... look.

The player is allowed to take it in.

Janine raises her phone again, instinctively trying to use it.

Phone screen texture:
NO SERVICE / spinner / failed load.

JANINE
Still nothing.
(beat)
Why do I still have no signal?

Nobody answers.

Tanya instinctively raises her phone toward the skyline as if to take a picture, then lowers it without pressing the shutter.

TANYA
That doesn’t look right.

Wind moves across the platform.

No music.

A long enough pause for unease to become discomfort.

SCENE 5 — THE SOUND

At first, just under the wind:

A low, uneven engine hum.

Not close enough yet to locate.
Not normal enough to ignore.

Louis hears it first. He turns away from the skyline and looks up and behind, trying to place the sound.

LOUIS
Do you hear that?

The player can turn view freely.

The hum builds. Heavy. Wrong pitch. Too low.

BYSTANDER 1
What is that?

VERONICA
Is that a plane?

BYSTANDER 2
That’s way too low.

The sound grows very fast.

SCENE 6 — AIRLINER PASS

A brief, instinctive upward camera pull.

Through partial tree cover overhead, the player catches only a broken glimpse of a large commercial airliner passing far too low and at the wrong angle.

It is not a full reveal.
It is only enough to understand what it is and that it should not be there.

The plane roars past and out of sight.

JANINE
Oh my God—

LOUIS
That is low—

TANYA
Why is it—

The plane is gone.

Silence.

One beat.

Two.

Then, from the distance:

A deep, hollow impact boom.

No visible fireball.
Just the sound.

Everything changes.

SCENE 7 — PANIC BREAK

The bystanders react in staggered fashion.

One ducks.
Another swears.
Another backs away.
Then motion spreads.

BYSTANDER 2
Jesus Christ—

BYSTANDER 1
Did that just crash?

VERONICA
Oh my God.

Louis has already turned back toward the trail.

LOUIS
Guys. We gotta go. Now.

TANYA
Go where?

LOUIS
Back to the car. Move.

A new objective appears:

GET BACK TO THE CAR

SPRINT ENABLED.

Only now does music enter, if used at all: low, restrained, pulsing.

SCENE 8 — THE DESCENT

EXT. TRAIL BACK TO PARKING LOT — CONTINUOUS

The group runs downhill.

The same trail that felt scenic now feels narrow, crowded, and exposed.

Breathing.
Footfalls.
Leaves and brush snapping underfoot.
Shouts from other visitors moving in both panic and confusion.

Dialogue overlaps. Nobody is calm now.

TANYA
Wait— wait—

LOUIS
Come on!

JANINE
I dropped it— damn it—

VERONICA
Just keep moving!

At one point Janine fumbles and drops her phone onto the trail.
It skids into leaves.

She half-turns toward it on reflex.

JANINE
My phone—

TANYA
Leave it!

LOUIS
Janine, move!

Janine leaves it and runs.

A beat later, upset and breathless:

JANINE
I don’t even have my phone—

VERONICA
Just move!

Other visitors are heard around them, mostly off-screen:

OTHER VISITOR (O.S.)
What happened?

OTHER VISITOR 2 (O.S.)
Get in the car!

OTHER VISITOR 3 (O.S.)
Was that in the city?

OTHER VISITOR 4 (O.S.)
I can’t get my wife—

No nearby drones.
No gunfire.
Danger remains undefined.

SCENE 9 — PARKING LOT

EXT. TRAILHEAD PARKING LOT — CONTINUOUS

The group bursts out of the trees into the lot.

The area is destabilizing but not yet full riot:
Car doors slamming.
Engines starting.
People yelling across rows of cars.
Someone backing out too fast.
A child crying somewhere off-screen.
Someone frozen, staring at a dead phone screen.

Objective remains:

GET BACK TO THE CAR

The group runs to Louis’ vehicle:
An older three-row SUV, effectively analog — a late-1990s full-size Chevy Suburban type, old enough to have no networked systems worth speaking of.

Louis reaches the driver’s side first.

LOUIS
Come on, come on—

Doors open fast.

The player enters the front passenger seat.

CUT TO:

SCENE 10 — INSIDE THE SUV

INT. SUV — CONTINUOUS

First-person in the front passenger seat.

Door slam.
Seatbelt chime.
The key turns.
The engine catches immediately.

Good.
No hesitation.
No electronics acting up.

That little success matters.

Louis throws the vehicle into gear.

Tanya is breathing hard in the back. Veronica looks over her shoulder out the rear side window. Janine pats her pockets on reflex, realizes again the phone is gone, and looks suddenly at a loss.

TANYA
Go, go.

VERONICA
Just drive.

JANINE
I left it. I left my phone—

TANYA
Janine—

JANINE
I don’t have it. I don’t have anything.

The line should not sound melodramatic. More stunned than theatrical. She has lost the object she kept using to mediate the day.

Louis pulls toward the parking lot exit.

The player has LOOK CONTROL ONLY.

No objective text now.

Only tension.

SCENE 11 — THE EXIT ROAD

EXT./INT. PARKING LOT EXIT ROAD — CONTINUOUS

The SUV reaches the lot exit and slows just enough to check the road.

A car passes.

Then, almost immediately, another vehicle enters frame at unnatural speed and slams hard into it.

Metal folds.
Glass bursts.
The impact is shocking and abrupt.

Everyone in the SUV flinches.

A beat.

Then a second nearly identical vehicle rams into the wreck.

Not random panic driving.
Not an ordinary pileup.
Pattern.

From the passenger seat, the player sees enough through shattered glass and movement to register what is wrong:
No visible driver movement.
A blank-looking front seat.
Uncanny acceleration.
Near-identical vehicle profile.

Inside the SUV:

VERONICA
What the hell—

JANINE
There’s nobody in that car—

TANYA
Louis—

Louis stares ahead.

Quietly, almost to himself:

LOUIS
No.

Hold exactly long enough for the player to understand the meaning of that word.

Cut to black.

END.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
END SOURCE CONTENT

HUDSON OVERLOOK
Mission Scripting Document

Purpose
Cold-open interactive narrative sequence showing PANDORA from civilian ground level before the main campaign. The sequence must establish civilian-scale dread, introduce systemic/autonomous threat without explanation, and transition cleanly into Game 1 at the moment of recognition.

Core Intent
- Single continuous sequence, not montage
- First-person anonymous civilian POV
- Player agency limited to movement, looking, and staying with group
- No score until the run back to the car
- Cut at recognition, not aftermath

Sequence Metadata
Mission ID: NAR_COLDOPEN_HUDSON_OVERLOOK
Runtime Target: 6–8 minutes
Mode: Interactive-linear
Failure State: Soft leash only; no death/fail state in normal flow
Transition Out: Hard cut to black on Louis line “No.”

NPC Roster
NPC_TANYA
Role: emotional anchor / warmth -> fear

NPC_LOUIS
Role: perceptive lead / first to notice wrongness / driver

NPC_JANINE
Role: phone dependency / practical problem voice / loss-of-device beat

NPC_VERONICA
Role: quieter observer / stabilizing group voice during panic

PLAYER
Role: unnamed civilian / first-person / limited agency witness

Gameplay State Overview
STATE_00_BOOT
STATE_01_PICNIC
STATE_02_TRAIL_WALK
STATE_03_SIGNAL_BEAT
STATE_04_APPROACH
STATE_05_OVERLOOK_REVEAL
STATE_06_ENGINE_SOUND
STATE_07_AIRLINER_PASS
STATE_08_PANIC_BREAK
STATE_09_DESCENT
STATE_10_PARKING_LOT
STATE_11_SUV_INTERIOR
STATE_12_EXIT_IMPACT
STATE_13_CUT_TO_BLACK

Music Logic
MUSIC_NONE from STATE_00 through STATE_07
MUSIC_LOW_PULSE begins at STATE_08 only
MUSIC_STOP on cut to black

HUD Logic
Minimal narrative HUD only
Allowed prompts:
- [STAND UP]
- FOLLOW YOUR FRIENDS
- GET BACK TO THE CAR
No tactical HUD, no enemy markers, no waypoint chevrons if avoidable
Use soft environmental guidance instead

CAMERA / CONTROL RULES
- Standard first-person throughout except for brief scripted head motion on stand and on airliner pass
- No third-person insert shots
- Look control available in every state
- Walk enabled from STATE_02 onward
- Sprint disabled until STATE_08
- Interaction prompts minimal, single-button where needed
- No weapon, inventory, or combat systems exposed

----------------------------------------------------------------
Purpose
Fade in from black and establish ordinary day-off tone.

OnEnter
- Fade in from black over 1.5 sec
- Load ambient trailhead soundscape
- Set player seated at picnic table anchor
- Look control only
- Disable walk, sprint, interaction except stand prompt
- No music

Transition Condition
- 3–5 seconds elapsed and opening tableau fully loaded

- Tanya instinctively raises phone to frame skyline
- She lowers it without taking a photo
VO_TANYA_017: “That doesn’t look right.”

Transition Condition
- Minimum dwell met
- Player orientation enters audio trigger sector ATS_ENGINE_LISTEN or dwell timer expires

Next State
STATE_06_ENGINE_SOUND

----------------------------------------------------------------
STATE_06_ENGINE_SOUND
----------------------------------------------------------------
Purpose
Introduce offscreen airliner through sound first.

OnEnter

- Hum pans ambiguously then resolves overhead trajectory
- Bystander and Louis attention redirection from skyline to sky/behind

VO_BYSTANDER_003: “What is that?”
VO_VERONICA_006: “Is that a plane?”
VO_BYSTANDER_004: “That’s way too low.”

- Hum ramps from -18 dB to near pass level over 6–8 sec
- Avoid clean commercial flyover signature; pitch instability desirable

Transition Condition
- Hum reaches peak threshold OR 7 sec elapsed

Next State

STATE_07_AIRLINER_PASS

- Important: do not show full glamour shot; only broken glimpse sufficient for recognition

VO_TANYA_018: “Why is it—”

- Then immediate offscreen departure
- 2 sec silence

- Crash boom complete

Next State
STATE_12_EXIT_IMPACT

----------------------------------------------------------------
STATE_12_EXIT_IMPACT
----------------------------------------------------------------
Purpose
Deliver final realization image: autonomous pattern, not random panic.

Player Control
- Look only
- Vehicle remains stopped/creeping at exit

OnEnter
- Spawn/drive civilian road car through crossing path
- After 0.8–1.2 sec spawn autonomous impact car at unnatural acceleration
- Collision 1: autonomous vehicle rams passing car
- Hold 0.7–1.0 sec
- Collision 2: near-identical autonomous vehicle rams the wreck

Visual Requirements
- Enough readability to imply no active driver / empty front seat / uncanny system behavior
- Similar silhouette between impact vehicles
- Should read as pattern, not conventional pileup

SFX
- High-impact metal fold
- Glass burst
- Tire scrub minimal; more committed acceleration than evasive driving

Dialogue
VO_VERONICA_011: “What the hell—”
VO_JANINE_019: “There’s nobody in that car—”
VO_TANYA_024: “Louis—”
VO_LOUIS_016: “No.”

Hold Logic
- Hold 1.5–2.0 sec after VO_LOUIS_016
- Allow player to scan wreck just long enough for realization

Transition Condition
- Hold complete

Next State

----------------------------------------------------------------
DESIGN GUARDRAILS
----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Do not let the overlook beat move too fast.
   The dread comes from looking long enough to not understand.

2. Do not add explicit tech exposition.
   No one should say “PANDORA,” “autonomous system,” or anything intelligence-flavored.

3. Do not add nearby drones or gunfire before the road impact sequence.
   The threat should remain indeterminate through most of the scene.

4. Keep panic compressed once it starts.
   The return to the car should feel messy and urgent, not like a full survival level.

5. The road impacts are the thesis image.
   The airliner is shock; the cars are recognition.

6. The analog SUV must start cleanly.
   That moment matters thematically.

7. Cut on Louis’ “No.”
   Do not continue into another action beat.
